{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"13 Great Landing Page Examples You'll Want to Copy in 2020","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/fantastic-landing-page-examples","description":"<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">While many landing pages look different and use a variety of interesting strategies to pull in audiences, they all serve one major purpose. These pages get website visitors to convert to the next stage in <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/what-is-the-buyers-journey\">the buyer's journey</a>. </span></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\"></span></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">Rather than serving as a basic advertisement that shows a customer a product, a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-landing-page-builder\">landing page</a> aims to engage and delight a customer by offering them something that relates to the product or the company's industry. When they fill out the form and receive a reward of interesting content, they might be even more likely to trust your brand and become a customer.<br><br><strong>Quick tip:</strong> Want an easy way to add a form to your landing page? <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/forms\">HubSpot’s free form builder tool</a> can help you fill your CRM with leads from your website. <br></span></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">Let’s talk through an example of when a landing page can be especially effective. If a business wants to sell an AI product that helps salespeople, they might create a landing page that offers audiences a free video on how to use AI in the sales industry. Interested audiences might offer their contact information in exchange for the valuable information. If they enjoy the video they've received, they might be more likely to respond to or purchase a product from a company rep who calls them.</span></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">In another scenario, a publishing company that targets an audience of chief executives might create a landing page that invites audiences to sign up for a webinar hosted by an executive at a major company. </span></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">After giving their email address on the signup form presented on the landing page, the leads get an email with the webinar dates and log in information, as well as instructions on how to sign up for the publication's newsletter or subscription. If the user is pleased by the webinar, they might sign up for the newsletter or a subscription to keep up with similar publication content. </span></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">Although their purpose is simple enough in theory, actually designing a successful landing page requires some detailed planning and </span><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/design-website-experiments?_ga=2.259813322.1706660370.1562589600-1582690004.1559596502\" style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">creative testing</a><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">.</span></p> \n<p>Even after launching your landing page, you'll want to pay attention to conversion rates to see how well it's doing.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p><span>To determine your conversion rate, simply divide the number of conversions a webpage generates by the number of people who visited that page.</span></p> \n<p><span>If your conversion rate isn't close to the average just yet, don't worry. </span><a href=\"https://www.wordstream.com/blog/ws/2014/03/17/what-is-a-good-conversion-rate\">Nailing those percentages </a>can be a bit challenging at first, especially is you have a lot of regular page visitors. Luckily, there are a number of simple <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/conversion-rate-optimization-guide\">conversion rate optimization strategies</a> that can help you boost your current rate quickly.</p> \n<p>Regardless of what your business is selling or the conversion action you hope to instigate, it's helpful to get inspired by seeing what other great landing pages look like. And because there's no one \"right\" way of <a href=\"http://pearl.stylemixthemes.com/landing/\">designing a landing page</a>, you'll want to check out examples from lots of different industries for different stages of the buying process.</p> \n<p>Want to get inspired? Check out the great landing page examples below.</p> \n<p>We don't have access to the analytics for each of these landing pages, so I can't tell you specifically how well they convert visitors, contacts, leads, and customers. But many of them do follow best practices while also implementing a few new experiments that could give you ideas for your own landing pages.</p> \n<p></p> \n<h2>13 Great Examples of Landing Page Design</h2> \n<h3>1. <a href=\"https://www.lyft.com/drive-for-lyft\">Lyft</a></h3> \n<p>We love that on Lyft's landing page, they zero in on their drivers' main motivation: earning money easily.</p> \n<p>We also love that, in addition to the \"Apply Now\" form, drivers can type their city and the number of hours they might drive for Lyft in a week to calculate how much they'd make. When visitors fill out that information and press \"Calculate,\" they aren't taken to a new page. Instead, they see a dollar amount followed by a new call-to-action button to \"Apply Now\" (which, once clicked, takes drivers up to the form).</p> \n<p>By offering these two conversion paths, they're able to address two different types of people in the conversion path: those who are ready to make the decision now <em>and</em> those who need a little more information before they convert.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/lyft-landing-page.png?width=667&amp;height=501&amp;name=lyft-landing-page.png\" alt=\"lyft-landing-page\" width=\"667\" height=\"501\"></p> \n<h3>2. <a href=\"http://www.theprofessionalwingman.com/apply-for-coaching-1\">The Professional Wingman</a></h3> \n<p>Okay, so the whole idea of having a professional wingman to help you find dates and a meaningful relationship is already pretty cool. But when you're faced with the prospect of hiring one, it also raises questions. How does it work? How much does it cost? Is this really going to help me?</p> \n<p>That's why we love this landing page for Thomas Edwards, the original Professional Wingman himself, which outlines exactly what a complimentary coaching session is going to achieve. Plus, it's clear that it's complimentary, thanks to the boldly-colored call-to-action button above the fold.</p> \n<p>Once you click that button, you aren't taken to a new page. Instead, an interstitial form appears right there. And while it does request a lot of information -- some of it a bit personal -- it also sends the message that The Professional Wingman is going to take this seriously, but only if you do, too.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/professional%20wingman.gif?width=669&amp;name=professional%20wingman.gif\" alt=\"professional wingman landing page\" width=\"669\" title=\"professional wingman.gif\" style=\"width: 669px;\"></p> \n<h3>3. <a href=\"http://muckrack.com/\">Muck Rack</a></h3> \n<p>This landing page design has it all. It's visually appealing and interactive, offers scannable yet descriptive headers about Muck Rack's services, and uses quotes from industry professionals as social proof. Plus, the page is intuitive and easy to navigate.</p> \n<p>The cool part about this landing page is that it can appeal to both of Muck Rack's audiences. The top of the page is split into two, featuring their two different services side by side. Once a visitor moves his or her mouse over either of the \"find journalists\" or the \"build free portfolio\" CTAs, a very <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/forms\">simple form</a> appears -- and that's important, so as not to distract the user from the task at hand.</p> \n<p><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" style=\"width: 669px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/muckrack.gif?width=669&amp;name=muckrack.gif\" alt=\"muckrack landing page\" width=\"669\" title=\"muckrack.gif\"></p> \n<h3>4. <a href=\"https://www.cigital.com/resources/ebooks-and-whitepapers/security-threat-modeling-misconceptions/\">Cigital</a></h3> \n<p>There are a few things that make this Cigital landing page work. It has simple and relevant imagery. The headline is straightforward and the description of the ebook informs viewers of the specific value they will get by downloading it. There is only one call-to-action -- \"READ THE EBOOK\" -- that stands out on the page thanks to a bright yellow CTA button.</p> \n<p>The only thing we'd change about this landing page is that we'd remove the navigation bar at the top. They tend to distract visitors and lead them away from the intended action. Not only is this a landing page design best practice, but <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/landing-page-navigation-ht\">we've also conducted A/B tests</a> that've shown removing navigation links from landing pages increases conversion rates.</p> \n<p><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" style=\"width: 669px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Cigital.gif?width=669&amp;name=Cigital.gif\" alt=\"Cigital landing page\" width=\"669\" title=\"Cigital.gif\"></p> \n<h3>5. <a href=\"https://www.khanacademy.org/\">Khan Academy</a></h3> \n<p>The hard part about using your homepage as a landing page is that you have to cater to several different types of audiences. But Khan Academy's homepage does that very well. This page is clearly designed for three different types of visitors: those who want to learn something, those who want to teach, and parents who are interested in using Khan Academy for their kids. Plus, how motivational is the emblazoned \"You can learn anything\" text at the top?</p> \n<p>The remainder of the page is designed for viewers who are not completely familiar with Khan Academy. It colorfully and largely spells out the key benefits of using the learning platform -- all of which are easy to scan and understand. There's also a recurring CTA: \"Start learning now.\" As soon as viewers feel they have enough information, they can click the CTA to get taken back up to the form at the top of the page without having to scroll.</p> \n<p><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" style=\"width: 669px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/khan%20academy.gif?width=669&amp;name=khan%20academy.gif\" alt=\"khan academy landing page\" width=\"669\" title=\"khan academy.gif\"></p> \n<h3>6. <a href=\"https://clubw.com/gifts/corporate/\">Club W</a></h3> \n<p>A little bit of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33441/10-Companies-That-Totally-Nail-Copywriting.aspx\">delightful copy can go a long way</a> on your landing page. We love the playful little aside -- \"(Hint: It's Wine)\" -- that Club W included below the header of their corporate gifting landing page. It humanizes the brand and makes them likable, which could have a positive impact on their conversion rate.</p> \n<p>The images below that header make a nice use of negative space, showing the user exactly what his or her gift recipient might actually receive, should they choose to gift with Club W. And, of course, there's that bold call to action -- \"Email Us\".</p> \n<p>The one thing we'd change? The CTA prompts the users email software to open, which drives traffic away from the site and the browser entirely. A form might be more effective here -- not only would Club W be able to dictate what information it wants to capture, but also, it would keep the user on-site.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/club%20w.gif?width=669&amp;name=club%20w.gif\" style=\"width: 669px;\" width=\"669\" alt=\"club w landing page\" title=\"club w.gif\"></p> \n<h3>7. <a href=\"http://www.codecademy.com/\">Codecademy</a></h3> \n<p>I like this page because it's simple in both copy and design. The image above the fold is a computer screen displaying an HTML bracket with a blinking cursor -- a whimsical, clear visual to accompany the form on the right.</p> \n<p>The form itself is simple and only requires an email address, username, password, and a validation that you're not a robot to create an account. Or, you can just use your Facebook or Google Plus login, shortening the conversion path even further.</p> \n<p>For visitors who need more information before creating an account, the landing page also offers a video below the fold that explains their concept and value by way of a real-life success story. Again, this helps make the potentially intimidating world of coding more approachable for beginners.</p> \n<p>Those who need even more convincing can continue scrolling for additional testimonials and other forms of social proof.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><strong><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/codecademy.gif?width=669&amp;name=codecademy.gif\" alt=\"codecademy landing page\" width=\"669\" title=\"codecademy.gif\" style=\"width: 669px;\"></strong></p> \n<h3>8. <a href=\"https://poachedjobs.com/choose/\">Poached</a></h3> \n<p>I don't think we've ever lived in a time when, culturally, we've been so food-obsessed. Poached has turned that into a B2B model with a platform to connect proprietors and culinary talent.</p> \n<p>When you visit the homepage, there's no mystery about what you're there to do -- the giant \"Post a job\" and \"Choose a city\" calls to action help with that. And once you click on one of them, you're taken to a no-frills form to become a member or log in, or a list of jobs in each city. It's colorful and comprehensive -- and, it makes us hungry.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/poached.gif?width=669&amp;name=poached.gif\" alt=\"poached landing page\" width=\"669\" title=\"poached.gif\" style=\"width: 669px;\"></p> \n<h3>9. <a href=\"https://breather.com/\">Breather</a></h3> \n<p>Here's another example of clever, delightful design on a landing page. As soon as you visit Breather.com, there's an instant call to action: indicate where you want to find a space. Plus, it uses location services to figure out where you are, providing instant options nearby.</p> \n<p>We love how Breather used simple, to-the-point copy to let the visitor know what the company does, followed immediately by the CTA to select a city. And if you need to scroll down for more information, you can see that Breather <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/writing-great-microcopy\">played with the microcopy</a> with personality (\"no commitment, ever\"), reminding us there are real humans behind the design. That brings us a little closer to the brand. The negative space and soothing color scheme are also aligned with the product -- essentially, room to breathe.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/breather.gif?width=669&amp;name=breather.gif\" style=\"width: 669px;\" width=\"669\" alt=\"breather.gif\" title=\"breather.gif\"></p> \n<h3>10. <a href=\"https://www.startupinstitute.com/apply/\">Startup Institute</a></h3> \n<p>Visitors to your website won't hand over their personal information without knowing what they're going to get in return. On its landing page, Startup Institute makes abundantly clear what will happen after you apply by listing a Q&amp;A right beside the form. It might prompt some people to say, \"They read my mind!\"</p> \n<p>To avoid hesitancy to fill out a form, use your landing page to set expectations upfront. That clears the air, and can also weed out the people who don't take your content, product or service seriously.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Startup%20Institute.gif?width=669&amp;name=Startup%20Institute.gif\" width=\"669\" alt=\"Startup Institute landing page\" title=\"Startup Institute.gif\" style=\"width: 669px;\"></p> \n<h3>11. <a href=\"http://edupath.com/planding/PSO020414/\">Edupath</a></h3> \n<p>Who is your landing page's target audience? While most of Edupath's website content is directed toward students, there are sections dedicated to advising parents on helping their teenagers through college applications and SAT preparation. The landing page below is in one of these sections.</p> \n<p>When parents fill out their teenager's name, email address, and mobile number, a link to download the Edupath app is sent directly to them. The folks at Edupath know students are likely to do something if their parents ask them to -- especially if it means they don't have to surrender their phones.</p> \n<p>Plus, it's an easy, one-click process. This whole conversion path is a clever and helpful way to get the apps on more students' phones by way of their parents.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/edupath.gif?width=669&amp;name=edupath.gif\" width=\"669\" alt=\"edupath landing page\" title=\"edupath.gif\" style=\"width: 669px;\"></p> \n<h3>12. <a href=\"https://www.tastersclub.com/\">Taster's Club</a></h3> \n<p>If there's anything we enjoy more than a fine whiskey, it's a whiskey club homepage that makes it easy to either join or learn more about membership. Case in point: Taster's Club, which immediately serves up those very two CTAs on its landing page -- which also happens to be its homepage.</p> \n<p>For those to wish to learn more, clicking that CTA will immediately scroll the user down to colorful, image-rich details on what a Taster's Club membership includes. Keep scrolling, and you get user testimonials.</p> \n<p>But clicking the \"Join Now\" button is where the real fun begins. After doing that, you get to pick your poison -- that is, the type of whiskey you like the most -- and view the membership or gifting options available for it. Once you make your selections, you're taken to an easy-to-navigate checkout page to enter your payment information. Good design and ease of use? We'll drink to that.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/taster's%20club.gif?width=669&amp;name=taster's%20club.gif\" width=\"669\" alt=\"taster's club landing page\" title=\"taster's club.gif\" style=\"width: 669px;\"></p> \n<h3>13. <a href=\"https://info.microsoft.com/US-SCRTY-WBNR-FY19-06Jun-20-SpeakingofsecurityPrivacycompliance-1712_LP02OnDemandRegistration-ForminBody.html\">Microsoft IT Showcase</a></h3> \n<p>The landing page below has been used to market and generate leads for one episode of Microsoft's IT Showcase webinar series.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Microsoft%20IT%20Showcase%20Webinar%20Landing%20page.jpg?width=1449&amp;name=Microsoft%20IT%20Showcase%20Webinar%20Landing%20page.jpg\" alt=\"Microsoft IT Showcase Webinar Landing page\" width=\"1449\" style=\"width: 1449px;\"></p> \n<p>This simple and straightforward design does a great job of presenting why the webinar being offered is important to IT professionals. Along with a quick blurb describing what the webinar will discuss, the page also includes links to similar webinars, details on the speakers, and links to Microsoft resources that touch on the topics that will be discussed.</p> \n<p>An IT company which has access to thought leaders or experts in their industry could similarly use this webinar landing page strategy to generate both leads and prospective customer trust. Audiences who feel informed after reading the landing page might sign up expecting the webinar to be insightful.</p> \n<p>If the webinar seems informative and credible, these audiences will think that the IT company has an expertise in the product and might have quality product offerings. This will make them more willing to talk to a representative to learn more or purchase a product.</p> \n<h2>Ready to build your landing page?</h2> \n<p>If these examples have inspired you, but you're not a design expert, we've also created a great list of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/free-landing-page-templates\">free, professionally designed landing page templates</a>.</p> \n<p>If you're looking for more landing page design examples, check out some of our favorite <a href=\"https://academy.hubspot.com/examples#filter=.landing-page\">HubSpot landing page examples</a>. You can also check out <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/landing-page-design\">this quick guide to landing page design</a>.</p> \n<p><em></em></p> \n<div>\n <a class=\"close\"> </a>\n</div> "https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn98@2020_1/2020/11/14/17-30-27-547_767e2e6b7910f6bb.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/taster's%20club.gif?width=669&name=taster's%20club.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn1@2020_5/2020/11/14/17-30-32-883_6208f504e6e0bc66.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Microsoft%20IT%20Showcase%20Webinar%20Landing%20page.jpg?width=1449&name=Microsoft%20IT%20Showcase%20Webinar%20Landing%20page.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn51@2020_4/2020/11/14/17-30-21-912_e790cb48f7559403.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Ffantastic-landing-page-examples&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn30@2020_2/2020/11/14/17-30-21-655_a1acdf83112647ba.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605375018173},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"17 of the Best Examples of Beautiful Blog Design","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx","description":"<p>According to a recent <a href=\"https://www.affili.net/uk/about-affilinet/press-centre/2015/bloggers-trusted-more-than-celebrities-journalist\" style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">U.K. survey</a>, bloggers have ranked as the&nbsp;third most trustworthy source of information, following only friends and family. That's right -- bloggers are trusted more than celebrities, journalists, brands, and politicians.</p> \n<p>But how do you get people to fall in love with your blog in the first place? (Aside from remarkable content, of course.)</p> \n<p>Well, just as your <a title=\"website homepage\" href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34006/15-Examples-of-Brilliant-Homepage-Design.aspx\">website homepage</a> is like the front door to your business, your blog's design -- much like a welcome mat -- is the front door to your business blog.</p> \n<p>If you're not attracting people visually, how will you get them to take the next steps to actually read (and, hopefully, <a title=\"subscribe to\" href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33700/How-to-Convert-Casual-Blog-Visitors-Into-Dedicated-Subscribers.aspx\">subscribe to</a>) your content?&nbsp;Once you're done creating the&nbsp;quality content, you still have the challenge of presenting it in a way that clearly dictates&nbsp;what your blog is about. Images, text, and links need to be shown off just right -- otherwise, readers might abandon your content, if it's not showcased in a way that's appealing, easy to follow, and <a href=\"http://pearl.stylemixthemes.com/landing/\">generates more interest</a>.</p> \n<p>That's why we've compiled some examples of&nbsp;<a href=\"https://library.hubspot.com/blog-editorial-calendar\">blog</a> homepages to get you on the right track to designing the perfect blog for your readers. Check 'em out, below.</p> \n<p></p> \n<div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet\"> \n <h2>Beautiful Blog Examples to Inspire You</h2> \n <ol> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#helpscout\">Help Scout</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#microsoft\">Microsoft Stories</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#pando\">Pando</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#designmilk\">Design Milk</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#fubiz\">Fubiz</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#webdesigner\">Webdesigner Depot</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#mashable\">Mashable</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#brit\">Brit + Co</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#tesco\">Tesco Living</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#crew\">Crew</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#innocent\">Innocent Drinks</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#five500px\">500px</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#pixelgrade\">Pixelgrade</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#barkpost\">BarkPost</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#goodwill\">Goodwill Industries International</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#charity\">charity:water</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34143/12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx#johnny\">Johnny Cupcakes</a></li> \n </ol> \n</div> \n<p class=\"p1\"></p> \n<h2>17 Inspiring Examples of Beautiful Blog Homepage Design</h2> \n<a></a> \n<h3>1.&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.helpscout.net/blog/\">Help Scout</a><a href=\"http://www.helpscout.net/blog/\"></a></h3> \n<p>Sometimes, the best blog designs are also the simplest. Help Scout, makers of customer service software, uses a unique but minimalist design on its blog that we love -- it<span>&nbsp;limits the&nbsp;use of copy and visuals and embraces negative space.</span></p> \n<p>What we particularly like about this blog is its use of featured images for all posts, including a banner one at the top that highlights a recent or particularly popular entry. These icons are&nbsp;set in front of bright, block colors that catch the readers' eye and signal what the post is about. And it works -- everything about this&nbsp;blog's design says \"clean\" and \"readable.\"</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Help_Scout_Blog-2.png?width=671&amp;name=Help_Scout_Blog-2.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Help_Scout_Blog-2.png\" title=\"Help_Scout_Blog-2.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span>2.&nbsp;<a href=\"http://news.microsoft.com/stories/index.html\">Microsoft Stories</a><a href=\"http://news.microsoft.com/stories/index.html\"></a></span></span></h3> \n<p><span class=\"content-post__body\">Full disclosure: We've totally gushed over Microsoft's \"Stories\" microsite <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/microsoft-stories-editorial-process?_ga=1.66271790.1053898511.1470656920\">before</a>. We can't help it -- what better way to revitalize an old-school brand than with a blog that boasts beautiful, interactive, and inspiring branded content? Plus,&nbsp;the square layout of these&nbsp;stories&nbsp;<span class=\"content-post__body\">is</span>&nbsp;reminiscent of&nbsp;the Microsoft logo, which achieves a valuable <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/unexpected-companies-twitter-content#sm.0000e1w1nuwvbeo5sq61j1tim2kyj\">brand consistency</a>.</span></p> \n<p>Microsoft Stories is also a prime example of how a business blog can be a major asset for an overall rebrand. In recent years, Microsoft has worked to humanize its brand, largely in response to <a href=\"http://www.brandknewmag.com/index.php/the-ad-battle-between-apple-and-microsoft-is-back/\">a rivalry&nbsp;with Apple</a>. The \"Stories\" microsite has a simple tagline -- \"Get an inside look at the people, places and ideas that move us.\" It's the softer side of Microsoft, so to speak.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>When you're trying to convey a certain brand message, your blog can be used to communicate it -- both aesthetically, and content-wise.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/00-Blog_Thinkstock_Images/Microsoft_Stories_Blog.png?width=671&amp;name=Microsoft_Stories_Blog.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Microsoft_Stories_Blog.png\" title=\"Microsoft_Stories_Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></span></span></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>3.&nbsp;<a title=\"PandoDaily\" href=\"https://pando.com/\">Pando</a><a title=\"PandoDaily\" href=\"https://pando.com/\"></a></h3> \n<p>An important aspect of a well-designed blog is a consistent color scheme and style -- after all, <a href=\"http://www.webpagefx.com/blog/web-design/psychology-of-color-infographic/\">80% of consumers say that color boosts their recognition of a brand</a>.</p> \n<p>It's interesting to see how color consistency can unify the more diversified elements of design. Pando, a blog that explores the startup cycle, incorporates blue&nbsp;tones in several sections of its site -- the background, highlight bars, and certain areas of text. But it also uses several different fonts -- all of which manage to look seamless together,&nbsp;when tied together by a cohesive color scheme.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Pando_Blog.png?width=671&amp;name=Pando_Blog.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Pando_Blog.png\" title=\"Pando_Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>4.&nbsp;<a title=\"Design Milk\" href=\"http://design-milk.com/\">Design Milk</a><a title=\"Design Milk\" href=\"http://design-milk.com/\"></a></h3> \n<p>Design Milk, an online contemporary design outlet, uses a very simple layout to highlight its posts. The sidebar to the right -- which remains visible&nbsp;when a blog post is opened to read -- is perfect for showcasing&nbsp;thumbnail images for&nbsp;new articles. That's an <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/inbound-links-faqs#sm.0000e1w1nuwvbeo5sq61j1tim2kyj\">internal link</a> strategy, which helps to encourage readers to remain on the site longer.</p> \n<p>The social icons at the top are a pleasant addition to the overall look and feel of the site -- they're easy to spot, and make it easy to share Design Milk's content. (And to learn more about adding social buttons to your blog, check out&nbsp;<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/29544/The-Ultimate-Cheat-Sheet-for-Creating-Social-Media-Buttons.aspx\">this post</a>.)</p> \n<h4 style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_10.42.15_AM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_10.42.15_AM.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Design Milk Blog.png\" title=\"Design Milk Blog.png\" /></h4> \n<a></a> \n<h3><span class=\"content-post__body\">5.&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.fubiz.net/\">Fubiz</a><a href=\"http://www.fubiz.net/\"></a></span></h3> \n<p><span>Fubiz, an art and design blog, is an example of a&nbsp;really sleek design that also includes&nbsp;some cool personalization. </span></p> \n<p><span>Near the top of the blog's homepage, readers&nbsp;can side-scroll through \"highlighted\" posts. Below that is the Creativity Finder, where visitors&nbsp;can select their chosen&nbsp;personas -- from \"Art Lover\" to \"Freelance\" -- location, and the type of content they're looking for. From there, readers can browse content specifically catered to them.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span>We can't help but love the header image, too. It uses something called <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Blue-Mind-Surprising-Healthier-Connected/dp/0316252085\">\"blue mind\"</a> psychology, which has found that the sight of open water can naturally draw us in. By using it in a design scheme, Fubiz is able to visually attract visitors to its content.</span></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_10.45.16_AM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_10.45.16_AM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Fubiz blog.png\" title=\"Fubiz blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></span></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>6.&nbsp;<a title=\"Webdesigner Depot\" href=\"http://www.webdesignerdepot.com/\">Webdesigner Depot</a><a title=\"Webdesigner Depot\" href=\"http://www.webdesignerdepot.com/\"></a></h3> \n<p>With a name like \"Webdesigner Depot,\" it's no wonder that this design news site is visually appealing.</p> \n<p>One thing that we particularly like is the way Webdesigner Depot has incorporated social sharing icons on each individual post. While we of course suggest actually reading each piece, having those links readily available helps visitors immediately share a headline they find interesting. And check out those navigation arrows on the right -- never before has it been so easy to scroll to the top or bottom of a page.</p> \n<p>What's more, the color scheme, background, and fonts are all consistent -- which keeps this blog looking professional, but still distinct from the basic blog templates we&nbsp;might be&nbsp;used to seeing.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.00.18_AM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.00.18_AM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Webdesigner Depot Blog.png\" title=\"Webdesigner Depot Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>7.&nbsp;<a title=\"Mashable\" href=\"http://mashable.com/\">Mashable</a><a title=\"Mashable\" href=\"http://mashable.com/\"></a></h3> \n<p>I mean, just look at that header image. The bold colors, the wiring overlay, the gripping pupil and the contrasting text. It absolutely catches the reader's eye -- no pun intended.</p> \n<p>Mashable breaks its content into three noticeable sections on the homepage: New posts are listed on the left in the smallest sized thumbnails.&nbsp;\"What's Rising\" posts are displayed in the center column as large&nbsp;thumbnails, and the \"What's Hot\" posts are shown to the right, also as large thumbnails. This three-pronged approach to displaying content can help readers decide which kind of news matters to them the most -- the attention-grabbing top story, or other posts that are currently trending.</p> \n<p>Plus, we like&nbsp;that the number of shares is displayed in each post preview -- that's a great form of social proof.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.02.47_AM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.02.47_AM.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Mashable Homepage.png\" title=\"Mashable Homepage.png\" /></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>8.&nbsp;<a title=\"Brit + Co.\" href=\"http://www.brit.co/\">Brit + Co</a><a title=\"Brit + Co.\" href=\"http://www.brit.co/\"></a></h3> \n<p>Everything about the Brit + Co homepage says \"clean,\" \"warm,\" and \"welcoming.\" It's free of clutter, making the content more digestible, and the layout is extremely organized.</p> \n<p>We dig the seasonality of the site, too. I mean, avocado jack-o'-lanterns on the dawn of October? Adorable, and replete with a colorful, fun photo to illustrate the story's content.</p> \n<p>The subtle \"trending\" header also serves as a nice way to promote popular content, without being too in-you-face about it. Plus, with such great visuals, we took note of the nod to Pinterest -- that icon is important to include when your blog incorporates attractive imagery.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.10.58_AM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.10.58_AM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Brit+Co Blog.png\" title=\"Brit+Co Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\">9.&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.tescoliving.com/\">Tesco Living</a><a href=\"http://www.tescoliving.com/\"></a></span></span></h3> \n<p>We love the colorful, consistent design of Tesco Living, the blog site of British grocery chain Tesco.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Remember how we keep harping away at brand consistency? Check out the rhombus-like designs in the top banner -- that reflects the same ones that appear in Tesco's logo.</p> \n<p>What Tesco Living has achieved is a great balance of simplicity and boldness. The layout is extremely minimal, but it isn't dull. Warm and welcoming shades&nbsp;underscore each content category, and the photos add dashes of colors throughout the site. It's a great example of how the right imagery can achieve an appealing \"less-is-more\" appearance, especially if that fits in with your overall brand concept.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.16.35_AM.png?width=920&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.16.35_AM.png\" title=\"TescoBlog.png\" width=\"920\" alt=\"TescoBlog.png\" style=\"width: 920px;\" /></span></span></span></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3><span class=\"content-post__body\">10.&nbsp;<a href=\"http://blog.crew.co/\">Crew</a><a href=\"http://blog.crew.co/\"></a></span></h3> \n<p>Crew Backstage, the blog of the Crew platform for designers and developers, has a fabulously minimalist blog design, but quiet a unique one.</p> \n<p>Notice that, above the fold, it&nbsp;features one blog post with a large title, subtitle, and call-to-action to read more.</p> \n<p>To the left, there's an equally minimalist call-to-action that makes it easy for readers to connect with&nbsp;Crew, or learn more. Plus, there's that consistency again -- everything above the fold is the same shade of blue, which has been shown to <a href=\"http://www.webpagefx.com/blog/web-design/psychology-of-color-infographic/\">invoke brand trust</a>.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.30.28_AM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.30.28_AM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Crew Backstage Blog.png\" title=\"Crew Backstage Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></span></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>11.&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.innocentdrinks.co.uk/blog\">Innocent Drinks</a><a href=\"http://www.innocentdrinks.co.uk/blog\"></a></h3> \n<p>Not only <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34227/15-Businesses-to-Admire-for-Consistent-Stellar-Branding.aspx\">are the folks at Innocent Drinks great copywriters</a>, but the design of its&nbsp;blog is also a great reminder that blog designs&nbsp;don't have to get super fancy.</p> \n<p>Notice how the logo -- displayed in the upper left -- is simple, cartoonish, and almost delightfully child-like. It works for Innocent Drinks (hint: childhood innocence), and that brand presence is maintained throughout the company's blog.</p> \n<p>The&nbsp;colorful fonts, for example, match the logo and stay in line with the brand's&nbsp;casual, playful voice. We also like the easily-na<span class=\"content-post__body\">vigable</span>&nbsp;archive links on the left, which are complemented by the geometric social sharing buttons on the right.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.37.10_AM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.37.10_AM.png\" title=\"Innocent Drinks Blog.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Innocent Drinks Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>12.&nbsp;<a title=\"500px\" href=\"http://500px.com/blog\">500px</a><a title=\"500px\" href=\"http://500px.com/blog\"></a></h3> \n<p>Much like&nbsp;Crew, the photography blog, 500px, leads with&nbsp;one featured article and a big, bold, high-definition photo&nbsp;to draw the reader in. That makes is pretty clear what the blog is about -- it boasts valuable content on photography with gripping photography.</p> \n<p>Plus, how cool is it that the social links are right there, obviously displayed above the fold? They keep readers engaged with the content, and make it easy to share the photography&nbsp;-- and,&nbsp;<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/infographics-for-seo-strategy\">content with images is up to three times as likely to be shared on social media</a>.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.38.40_AM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.38.40_AM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"500px Blog.png\" title=\"500px Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>13. <a href=\"https://pixelgrade.com/ref/94/\">Pixelgrade</a></h3> \n<div> \n <span class=\" author-d-1gg9uz65z1iz85zgdz68zmqkz84zo2qoxvz75zz66zoz83zz80z5bhjtng7ex0z76zz83zutvxuz85ztyypjk\">Pixelgrade is a design studio that creates stunning WordPress themes for all sorts of creative people and small businesses.&nbsp;</span> \n</div> \n<div>\n  &nbsp; \n</div> \n<div> \n <span class=\" author-d-1gg9uz65z1iz85zgdz68zmqkz84zo2qoxvz75zz66zoz83zz80z5bhjtng7ex0z76zz83zutvxuz85ztyypjk\">Their blog page does a great job of highlighting one of their most recent or popular blog posts, alongside a clear call to action and a short excerpt. What I like best is that the design of the page is 100% in line with their brand and how they communicate on other channels as well, like </span> \n <span class=\"attrlink url author-d-1gg9uz65z1iz85zgdz68zmqkz84zo2qoxvz75zz66zoz83zz80z5bhjtng7ex0z76zz83zutvxuz85ztyypjk\"><a class=\"attrlink\" href=\"https://www.instagram.com/pixelgrade/\">Instagram</a></span> \n <span class=\" author-d-1gg9uz65z1iz85zgdz68zmqkz84zo2qoxvz75zz66zoz83zz80z5bhjtng7ex0z76zz83zutvxuz85ztyypjk\">, </span> \n <span class=\"attrlink url author-d-1gg9uz65z1iz85zgdz68zmqkz84zo2qoxvz75zz66zoz83zz80z5bhjtng7ex0z76zz83zutvxuz85ztyypjk\"><a class=\"attrlink\" href=\"https://www.facebook.com/pixelgrademedia/\">Facebook</a></span> \n <span class=\" author-d-1gg9uz65z1iz85zgdz68zmqkz84zo2qoxvz75zz66zoz83zz80z5bhjtng7ex0z76zz83zutvxuz85ztyypjk\">, or </span> \n <span class=\"attrlink url author-d-1gg9uz65z1iz85zgdz68zmqkz84zo2qoxvz75zz66zoz83zz80z5bhjtng7ex0z76zz83zutvxuz85ztyypjk\"><a class=\"attrlink\" href=\"https://twitter.com/pixelgrade\">Twitter</a></span> \n <span class=\" author-d-1gg9uz65z1iz85zgdz68zmqkz84zo2qoxvz75zz66zoz83zz80z5bhjtng7ex0z76zz83zutvxuz85ztyypjk\">.</span> \n</div> \n<div>\n  &nbsp; \n</div> \n<div> \n <span class=\" author-d-1gg9uz65z1iz85zgdz68zmqkz84zo2qoxvz75zz66zoz83zz80z5bhjtng7ex0z76zz83zutvxuz85ztyypjk\">You will have no problem in identifying their blog posts, among other content you might come across while scrolling on social media.</span> \n</div> \n<p><span><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Pixelgrade%20Blog.png\" /></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>14.&nbsp;<a title=\"Treehugger\" href=\"http://barkpost.com/\">BarkPost</a><a title=\"Treehugger\" href=\"http://barkpost.com/\"></a></h3> \n<p>It's no secret that <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/introducing-the-pet-program#sm.0000e1w1nuwvbeo5sq61j1tim2kyj\">we kind of like dogs here at HubSpot</a>. So when a blog dedicated to life as a dog owner came across our radar, it got our attention.</p> \n<p>BarkPost, the blog of canine subscription box company BarkBox, is a great example of design for a number of reasons. First, look how easy it is to subscribe -- the call to action is right there, above the featured content. The social share icons are easily noticeable, too -- and, of course, all in the brand-matching, trustworthy blue.</p> \n<p>We also like that BarkPost draws attention to its sister companies, all of which are owned under the Bark &amp; Co portfolio of brands. But at the same time,&nbsp;the blog&nbsp;doesn't hock its own products -- rather, it serves as an informational resource to dog parents and lovers alike.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.50.59_AM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_11.50.59_AM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"BarkPost Blog.png\" title=\"BarkPost Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>15.&nbsp;<a title=\"Salvation Army\" href=\"http://www.goodwill.org/category/blog/\">Goodwill Industries International</a><a title=\"Salvation Army\" href=\"http://www.goodwill.org/category/blog/\"></a></h3> \n<p>Who says nonprofit organizations can't blog? Nay, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blogging-advance-nonprofit-career-ways-to-get-started\">they </a><em><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blogging-advance-nonprofit-career-ways-to-get-started\">should</a> --&nbsp;</em>and Goodwill's clean, colorful navigation (again -- the trustworthy blue) draw the reader to the important elements of this blog.</p> \n<p>The posts are also neatly positioned and easily accessible to readers. And, visitors can pick the type of information that matters to them the most by choosing a topic from the drop-down menu on the top right.</p> \n<p>Finally, we love that there's a collaborative call to action in the introductory text that invites readers to contribute content to the Goodwill blog. After all, the organizations&nbsp;services have reached&nbsp;37 million people -- here's a way for them to share their stories, or invite donors to write about why they chose to support Goodwill.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_12.19.16_PM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_12.19.16_PM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Goodwill Blog.png\" title=\"Goodwill Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>16.&nbsp;<a title=\"Charity: Water\" href=\"http://www.charitywater.org/blog/\">charity: water</a><a title=\"Charity: Water\" href=\"http://www.charitywater.org/blog/\"></a></h3> \n<p>Keeping the nonprofit blogging train going is charity: water, which makes&nbsp;excellent use of&nbsp;high-quality photography.</p> \n<p>Recently, the organization redesigned its blog with a lengthy post dedicated to its 10-year anniversary. Using that opportunity to share its impact over the past decade, charity: water maintained a simplistic design with concise text and bright images from the anniversary event.</p> \n<p>Plus, there's a clear CTA to donate at the top of the page. Placing that above a story about charity: water's impact is a double-edged sword, by both inspiring people to contribute to the cause while making it easy to do so.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_12.25.14_PM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_12.25.14_PM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"charity water blog-1.png\" title=\"charity water blog-1.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_12.27.11_PM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_12.27.11_PM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"charity: water blog 2.png\" title=\"charity: water blog 2.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3><span class=\"content-post__body\">17.&nbsp;</span><a title=\"Johnny Cupcakes\" href=\"http://www.johnnycupcakes.com/blog/\">Johnny Cupcakes</a><a title=\"Johnny Cupcakes\" href=\"http://www.johnnycupcakes.com/blog/\"></a></h3> \n<p>To clear up any confusion, Johnny Cupcakes doesn't actually make cupcakes. It makes clothing. But the company&nbsp;has done a great job of playing up its brand's association with baked goods -- its blog uses the subdomain \"kitchen.\"</p> \n<p>Plus, the folks at Johnny Cupcakes know a thing or two about brand consistency across channels. Its blog's simple color scheme and matching fonts help to create a unified user experience from the shop to&nbsp;general content, all the while throwing in bold, colorful images to catch readers' attention.</p> \n<p>Also, visit the website and have a scroll -- we think it's pretty cool how the background images vary, but stay positionally&nbsp;static for each entry.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span class=\"content-post__body\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_12.31.34_PM.png?width=671&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_12.31.34_PM.png\" width=\"671\" alt=\"Johnny Cupcakes Blog.png\" title=\"Johnny Cupcakes Blog.png\" style=\"width: 671px;\" /></span></p> \n<p><em><span class=\"content-post__body\">Here are 15 more award-winning <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-website-designs-list\">website design examples</a>.</span></em></p> \n<p></p> \n<p></p> \n<img =Screen_Shot_2016-09-30_at_12.31.34_PM.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn65@2020_1/2020/11/14/17-30-22-914_b5bda7dfcd1f75e6.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fblog%2Ftabid%2F6307%2Fbid%2F34143%2F12-inspiring-examples-of-beautiful-blog-homepage-designs.aspx&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn1@2020_5/2020/11/14/17-30-21-481_bd57f0b205ac1b2e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605375018188},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"How to Build an Email List from Scratch: 10 Incredibly Effective Strategies","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/list-building","description":"<p>Did you know it costs <a href=\"https://www.invespcro.com/blog/customer-acquisition-retention/\" style=\"font-size: 1.1rem;\">five times more</a><span style=\"font-size: 1.1rem;\"> to attract a new customer, than to keep an existing one?</span></p>  \n<p>Focusing on customer retention is a valuable long-term solution for increased revenue and sustainable growth, but it’s not always easy to cultivate that kind of loyalty.</p> \n<p>When I think about the brands I like best, like J. Crew, Spotify, and SoulCycle, I know I’m not a loyal brand advocate because of their products alone. I can get cheaper clothes, music, and groceries from plenty of other places. Ultimately, I’m a brand advocate because I believe in what they promote and I feel invested in their stories, like SoulCycle’s: “We aspire to inspire. We inhale intention and exhale expectation.” I relate to their brand messaging.</p> \n<p>One of the ways J. Crew, Spotify, and SoulCycle cultivate customer loyalty is through valuable content. While there are many ways to do this, <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/email\">email marketing</a> is one of the most powerful ways to reach your target audience -- if done correctly.</p> \n<p>I subscribe to J. Crew’s email list to get their “Flash Sale: Midnight” offers. I subscribe to Spotify’s newsletter to receive special promotions. And I subscribe to SoulCycle’s emails to hear about unique classes happening near me.</p> \n<p>In short, I subscribe to their emails to get value.</p> \n<p>If you’re starting from zero, building an impressive email list can feel like an impossible feat. Here, we'll cover some high-quality strategies to build an email list from scratch. Best of all, these strategies are designed to cultivate a loyal email subscriber base, so you can use your emails to attract better long-term customers.</p> \n<h2><strong>How to Build an Email List From Scratch </strong></h2> \n<h3><strong>1. Create a personalized CTA (call-to-action) for each blog or landing page. </strong></h3> \n<p>HubSpot has found personalized calls-to-action have a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/personalized-calls-to-action-convert-better-data\">42% higher view-to-submission rate</a> than calls-to-action that are the same for all visitors -- that’s almost double your potential email subscribers.</p> \n<p>It makes sense: the people who visit your blog post or web page are looking for something specific, so your CTA needs to meet those unique needs. For instance, if you’ve got a ton of traffic visiting your “List-Building Strategy” blog article, why not entice those people to subscribe to your email list by including a simple CTA like this: “Click here to download a free list-building toolkit.”</p> \n<p>Of course, personalized CTAs only work if you have the resources to create that quality content in the first place, but that process doesn’t have to be expensive or time-consuming. Instead of a toolkit, you could also offer an e-book, a fun quiz, or an exclusive article from your CEO on list-building strategies.</p> \n<p>If you offer content directly related to your visitor’s needs, your email newsletter won’t feel like a gimmicky advertisement. Instead, it will feel helpful and valuable -- key principles for a long-term customer retention plan.</p> \n<h3><strong>2. Create a pop-up or slide-in for each page of your site. </strong></h3> \n<p>A pop-up might sound initially bothersome, but I’m not talking about those early 2000 pop-up’s that promised you’d “Become a Model NOW”.</p> \n<p>Instead, I’m talking about timed pop-up ads, or onsite retargeting. After a user spends a certain amount of time on your page, she can receive a pop-up relevant to the content on that page, or to her behavior. Examples include exit pop-ups, which appear when a user tries to leave the page, or scroll pop-ups, which appear after the user scrolls a certain percentage down the page.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.optimonk.com/blog/test-results-digital-marketer-generated-2689-leads-14-days-using-onsite-retargeting/#.WzO-H9hKjOQ\">Digital Marketer conducted a case study</a> to determine the value of onsite retargeting. For one experiment in particular, Digital Marketer introduced a pop-up ad to returning visitors only, which appeared after a visitor spent 15 seconds on their site:</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/How%20to%20Build%20an%20Email%20List%20from%20Scratch%2010%20Incredibly%20Effective%20Strategies-1.png\" alt=\"\">\n</div> \n<p>Digital Marketer ensured this pop-up didn’t show up if someone came to the page from the newsletter (in which case, they were already signed up), and also didn’t pop-up on a sales page (which could interrupt someone’s purchasing decision).</p> \n<p>As you can see, Digital Marketer also took the time to offer meaningful content, a digital marketing toolbox, in their pop-up ad. With an impressive offer, your pop-up is no longer obtrusive or interruptive -- it’s simply helpful.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, their campaign generated <a href=\"https://www.optimonk.com/blog/test-results-digital-marketer-generated-2689-leads-14-days-using-onsite-retargeting/#.WzO-H9hKjOQ\">2,689 leads in two weeks, and increased their average time on page by 54%</a>. Pop-ups aren’t always gimmicky, and if done right, you’re able to appeal to your visitor with quality content when and where they need it.</p> \n<h3><strong>3. Create a timed pop-up survey. </strong></h3> \n<p>Most people don’t visit a new website and think, “Huh, so where’s the email sign-up form?” Often times, you need your viewers to feel invested in your content before you present them with a request for their emails.</p> \n<p>To build your email list, you might want to reach out to visitors on specific pages with surveys related to that content. I’m more willing to answer an “A or B” survey question if I’m already invested in the content -- it feels like a fairer trade-off.</p> \n<p>For instance, University of Alberta’s email subscriber list <a href=\"https://neilpatel.com/blog/a-little-nudge/\">grew almost 500% </a>in one year alone, thanks to a timed pop-up survey they implemented:</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/How%20to%20Build%20an%20Email%20List%20from%20Scratch%2010%20Incredibly%20Effective%20Strategies.png\" alt=\"\">\n</div> \n<p>The University of Alberta’s pop-up survey only appears after a visitor remains on a news’ page for 10 seconds. At that point, the viewers’ seen some value from the content, so ideally they’re more inclined to sign up for emails from the source.</p> \n<p>The University of Alberta’s survey pop-up is also one of the easiest forms I’ve ever seen. You enter your email and you’re done. People are often deterred from signing up when the form is too long and they don’t have the time, so a simple yes or no question might be your best bet for growing your email list.</p> \n<h3><strong>4. Use humor or sarcasm in your CTA’s “no, thanks” copy. </strong></h3> \n<p>We’re so infiltrated with “Yes or No” web offers on a daily basis, we barely see them anymore. To increase your email lists, you might want to try injecting some personality into your CTA copy.</p> \n<p>I always pause and laugh when I see a CTA with a small, “No thanks, I don’t want to lose weight,” button underneath a prominent “Yes, sign me up!” link. It reminds me there’s a person behind the button, and, while it’s meant to be a joke, it also incentivizes me to hesitate before clicking “no, thanks”. It’s easy to click “no” when the CTA is “sign up for more emails!”, but it’s a little harder to say no to losing weight or getting richer.</p> \n<p>I was reading an <a href=\"https://www.optimonk.com/\">Optimonk</a> blog post recently, and this CTA popped up:</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/How%20to%20Build%20an%20Email%20List%20from%20Scratch%2010%20Incredibly%20Effective%20Strategies-2.png\" alt=\"\">\n</div> \n<p>I was all set to click “No” without another thought, when I read the “my business isn’t important” part. It gave me pause, made me laugh, and, most importantly, made me reconsider my almost immediate decision to exit the offer.</p> \n<h3><strong>5. Describe value in your CTA. </strong></h3> \n<p>We’ve talked a lot about different formatting you might use in your CTA’s (including pop-up ads or personalized offers embedded in blog posts), but what about the language in the CTA itself? You can rely on more than humor and sarcasm to get clicks.</p> \n<p>To optimize sign-ups, ironically, you don’t want to use the words “sign up.” Who wants to “sign up” or “subscribe” to more junk emails? Instead, you want to outline the value you can offer upfront, using language like, “Download,” “Featured”, “Exclusive,” “Access.”</p> \n<p>For instance, you might write, “Download our exclusive e-book now,” and include an email subscription form, or, you might say, “Access all our exclusive offers.” Both of these CTAs make clear the value you’ll gain from providing your email address.</p> \n<p>Your web viewers need to hear how your emails can offer unique and exclusive content that isn’t already available on your website. They want to believe your company is offering something special via email, or what’s the point?</p> \n<h3><strong>6. Pitch your email newsletter on your social media accounts and email signature.</strong></h3> \n<p>You might not have a long list of email subscribers, but that doesn’t mean you don't have a network. If you have a following on Twitter, a fan base on Facebook, or businesses you communicate with via email, why not use those firm and loyal connections to build an email list?</p> \n<p>You might try pitching an email newsletter on your business’s Facebook, Twitter, or LinkedIn accounts. The people who follow you on those sites already know they like you, but they aren’t necessarily the same people who receive your newsletter. Give them the option.</p> \n<p>If you’re uncomfortable pitching your email newsletter on social media, or if you don’t have a large following on any of your accounts, you could also include a link in your email signature -- that link could go directly to your email newsletter, or it could be a link to a blog post or <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-landing-page-builder\">landing page</a> with email subscription CTA’s.</p> \n<p>You communicate daily with a diverse group of people via email, and when they get value from your personal emails, they might want the option to click a link and explore your company in more depth.</p> \n<h3><strong>7. Create more landing pages. </strong></h3> \n<p>HubSpot conducted research and found companies see a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33756/why-you-yes-you-need-to-create-more-landing-pages.aspx\">55% increase in leads</a> when you increase the number of landing pages from 10 to 15.</p> \n<p>It makes sense: individual and <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/landing-pages\">personalized landing pages</a> allow you to appeal to a wider demographic. Every person who visits your site needs something different, so the more landing pages you can create to answer each person’s individual concerns, the more sign-ups you’ll gain.</p> \n<p>It’s like a restaurant menu. The more you can offer to cater for specific demographics, the more customers you’ll bring in. Someone could be looking for the best gluten-free pizza, while someone else might just want some good sushi.</p> \n<h3><strong>8. Encourage everyone to sign up immediately. </strong></h3> \n<p>You want to strategically place personalized CTAs where it counts -- on landing pages and blog posts. But what about the rare, but real, visitors who want to sign up immediately?</p> \n<p>If your newsletter primarily centers around one or two topics, it’s relatively easy to create a personalized CTA -- simply write a CTA that mirrors your newsletter’s purpose, such as, “Want free SEO hacks? Sign up for our newsletter!”</p> \n<h3><strong>9. Include a CTA on your About Us page. </strong></h3> \n<p>Your About Us page is one of the most potent pages in terms of conversion potential. Think about it -- how often do you visit About Us pages for businesses you don’t care about?</p> \n<p>Ideally, your About Us page will prime visitors to want more from your business, but it might not be enough to convince them to purchase. A CTA that encourages them to sign up for a newsletter is easier to concede to than a “buy now” plea.</p> \n<h3><strong>10. Try a scroll box. </strong></h3> \n<p>Timing is everything. Your call-to-action works best if you catch visitors when they are, in fact, ready to take action.</p> \n<p>Figuring out when your visitor is ready to convert depends on your website viewers’ behavior, so you’ll want to conduct A/B testing to determine where you need to place your CTA. Does it work best towards the bottom of a blog page, when it slides out to the right, or does it get higher conversions at the beginning of the page, sliding out from the left?</p> \n<p>Ultimately, it will vary depending on your page’s content and your viewers, but a scroll box is a subtle and useful option to help you catch your viewers when they’re most ready to convert.</p> \n<p></p> \n<div>\n <a class=\"close\">&nbsp;</a>\n</div>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Flist-building&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\"
