ompany.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn50@2020_1/2020/11/14/17-30-22-113_2fbd20bc59679ae7.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Agency_Post/Blog_Images/scatter-plot-customer-happines.png?width=669&name=scatter-plot-customer-happines.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn39@2020_4/2020/11/14/17-30-20-817_aa69f677105b2d10.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Agency_Post/Blog_Images/bubble-chart.png?width=669&name=bubble-chart.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn22@2020_1/2020/11/14/17-30-21-866_d4c6e56f23127677.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Agency_Post/Blog_Images/waterfall-chart.png?width=669&name=waterfall-chart.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn57@2020_2/2020/11/14/17-30-23-925_f7d7b829c5f9ddf4.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Agency_Post/Blog_Images/DataHero_Marketing_Funnel.png?width=669&name=DataHero_Marketing_Funnel.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn29@2020_4/2020/11/14/17-30-20-755_8ec91d2cc19ceeac.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Agency_Post/Blog_Images/bullet-graph3.png?width=500&name=bullet-graph3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn18@2020_4/2020/11/14/17-30-23-547_126b773848f861db.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Agency_Post/Blog_Images/heat-map-chart.png?width=669&name=heat-map-chart.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn38@2020_6/2020/11/14/17-30-21-869_2e5bd26d95c58018.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Ftypes-of-graphs-for-data-visualization&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn62@2020_4/2020/11/14/17-30-24-825_ec0ac0ecc7ec24c4.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605375018203},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"The Ultimate Guide to Branding in 2020","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/branding","description":"<p>Products are never <em>just</em> products, right?</p> \n<p>Coca-Cola is more than a soda. Starbucks is more than a coffee. Ray-Ban is more than a pair of sunglasses. Glossier is more than a tube of concealer.</p> \n<p>Interacting with these products provide <em>experiences</em>, and we buy them with that experience in mind. Better yet, the companies that create and market them know exactly the experience they want you to have when you make (or consider) a purchase. <strong>That’s why they create a brand.</strong></p> \n<p>From the language in their Instagram caption to the color palette on their latest billboard to the material used in their packaging, companies who create strong brands know that their brand needs to live <em>everywhere</em>. They know their names extend far beyond the label.</p> \n<p>The result? These brands are known, loved, and chosen out of a long lineup of options.</p> \n<p>Who doesn’t want that? I know I do. That’s why we built this guide — to equip you to create and manage a strong brand that’ll help your business be admired, remembered, and preferred.</p> \n<p>Use the links below to jump ahead to sections of interest, and don’t forget to bookmark this guide for later.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p></p> \n<h2>What’s a brand?</h2> \n<p>Before I dive into the importance of branding and how to build a brand, let’s go back to basics: What is a brand?</p> \n<p>A <strong>brand</strong> is a feature or set of features that distinguish one organization from another. A brand is typically comprised of a name, tagline, logo or symbol, design, brand voice, and more. It also refers to the overall experience a customer undergoes when interacting with a business — as a shopper, customer, social media follower, or mere passerby.<a></a></p> \n<h2>What is branding?</h2> \n<p><strong>Branding</strong> is the process of researching, developing, and applying a distinctive feature or set of features to your organization so that consumers can begin to associate your brand with your products or services.</p> \n<p>Branding is an iterative process and requires getting in touch with the heart of your customers and your business. It’s important for a variety of reasons — I dive into these next.<a></a></p> \n<p></p> \n<p>Branding <strong>can be the deciding factor for consumers</strong> when they make a purchase decision. In <a href=\"https://www.nielsen.com/us/en/insights/news/2015/understanding-the-power-of-a-brand-name.html\">a 2015 global Nielsen survey</a>, almost 60% of shoppers said they actively buy from brands they know, and 21% said they bought a product because they liked the brand.</p> \n<p>Branding <strong>gives your business an identity</strong> beyond its product or service. It gives consumers something to relate to and connect with.</p> \n<p>Branding <strong>makes your business memorable</strong>. It’s the face of your company and helps consumers distinguish your business <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/branding#work\">across every medium (which I discuss later)</a>.</p> \n<p>Branding <strong>supports your marketing </strong>and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/advertising\">advertising efforts</a>. It helps your promotion pack that extra punch with added recognition and impact.</p> \n<p>Branding <strong>brings your employees pride</strong>. When you brand your company, you’re not only giving your business identity, you’re also creating a reputable, highly-regarded workplace. Strong branding brings in strong employees.<a></a></p> \n<h3>Branding Terms to Know</h3> \n<p>Here are some other brand-related buzzwords you should know. They further demonstrate the importance and value of branding your business.</p> \n<h4>Brand awareness</h4> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/brand-awareness\">Brand awareness</a> refers to how familiar the general public and your target audience is with your brand. High brand awareness leads to brands being referred to as “trending,” “buzzworthy, or “popular.” Brand awareness is important because consumers can’t consider purchasing from your brand if they’re not aware of it.</p> \n<p><em><span class=\"emoji\"><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/emojis\">👉🏼</a>&nbsp;</span>Strong branding makes your business known.</em></p> \n<h4>Brand extension</h4> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/brand-extensions\">Brand extensions</a> are when companies “extend” their brand to develop new products in new industries and markets. Consider <a href=\"http://powerequipment.honda.com/lawn-mowers\">Honda lawn mowers</a> or <a href=\"https://www.macys.com/shop/for-the-home/martha-stewart-bedding-bath?id=60363\">Martha Stewart bedding</a>. Brand extensions allow companies (or individuals) to leverage brand awareness and equity to create more revenue streams and diversify product lines.</p> \n<p><em><em><span class=\"emoji\">👉🏼</span></em> Strong branding brings in more money.</em></p> \n<h4>Brand identity</h4> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/agency/develop-brand-identity\">Brand identity</a> is the personality of your business and the promise you make to your customers. It’s what you want your customers to walk away with after they interact with your brand. <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34238/the-marketer-s-guide-to-developing-a-strong-brand-identity.aspx\">Your brand identity</a> is typically comprised of your values, how you communicate your product or service, and what you want people to feel when they interact with it.</p> \n<p><em><em><span class=\"emoji\">👉🏼</span></em>&nbsp;Strong branding gives your business more than a name.</em></p> \n<h4>Brand management</h4> \n<p>Brand management refers to the process of creating and maintaining your brand. It includes managing the tangible elements of your brand (style guide, packaging, color palette) and the intangible elements (how it's perceived by your target audience and customer base). Your brand is a living, breathing asset, and it should be managed as such.</p> \n<p><em><em><span class=\"emoji\">👉🏼</span></em>&nbsp;Strong branding requires consistent upkeep.</em></p> \n<h4>Brand recognition</h4> \n<p>Brand recognition is how well a consumer (ideally in your target audience) can recognize and identify your brand <em>without</em> seeing your business name — through your logo, tagline, jingle, packaging, or advertising. This concept goes hand-in-hand with <em>brand recall</em>, which is the ability to think of a brand without any visual or auditory identifiers.</p> \n<p><em><em><span class=\"emoji\">👉🏼</span></em> Strong branding keeps your business top-of-mind.</em></p> \n<p><strong>Real-life brand example</strong>: Want to test your brand knowledge? Take this <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/logo-quiz-can-you-identify-these-brands-when-their-names-are-stripped-out-2012-7\">Logo Quiz by Business Insider</a> to see how well you know your corporate brands. This is brand recognition at work.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/branding-6.png?width=600&amp;name=branding-6.png\" alt=\"branding-6\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\" /></p> \n<h4>Brand trust</h4> \n<p>Brand trust refers to how strongly customers and consumers believe in your brand. Do you deliver on your marketing promises? Do your salespeople and customer service go above and beyond? These things can create trust among your customers, which is important in a world where <a href=\"https://news.gallup.com/poll/1597/confidence-institutions.aspx\">a mere 25% of people</a> feel confident in large businesses.</p> \n<p><em><em><em><span class=\"emoji\">👉🏼</span></em></em>&nbsp;Strong branding builds trust with your customers.</em></p> \n<h4>Brand valuation</h4> \n<p>Brand valuation is the commercial valuation of your brand derived from consumer perception, recognition, and trust. This concept goes hand-in-hand with <em>brand equity</em>. A powerful brand can make your business invaluable to investors, shareholders, and potential buyers.</p> \n<p><em><em><em><span class=\"emoji\">👉🏼</span></em></em>&nbsp;Strong branding increases your business’s value.</em></p> \n<p><em>Want to build an effective, measurable brand? Download our free guide on <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/how-to-build-a-brand?hubs_post-cta=pillar_kwphrase\">How to Build a Brand in 2019</a>.</em></p> \n<div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet\"> \n <div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet__wrapper\"> \n  <h2><a></a>How to Create a Brand</h2> \n  <div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet__wrapper--content\"> \n   <ol> \n    <li>Determine your target audience</li> \n    <li>Establish your mission statement</li> \n    <li>Define your values, features, and benefits</li> \n    <li>Create your visual assets</li> \n    <li>Find your brand voice</li> \n    <li>Put your branding to work</li> \n   </ol> \n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<p>Here’s how you can <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/brand-your-business-on-a-budget\">create a brand</a> — or begin the process of rebranding your current one.</p> \n<p>There’s a lot that goes into a brand, and there’s a lot to consider when building a <em>strong</em> one. So, grab a notebook and jot down ideas as you move through this section. Recognize that branding is an iterative process, so you might be repeating some of these steps as you brainstorm and build your brand.</p> \n<h3>1. Determine your target audience</h3> \n<p>Branding leads to awareness, recognition, trust, and revenue. We’ve talked about that. But let’s take a step back and understand where those stem from: consumers. And not just any consumers — your target audience and customers.</p> \n<p>If your brand doesn’t resonate with your audience, it won’t lead to that awareness, recognition, trust, and revenue. That’s where <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/market-research-buyers-journey-guide\">target market research</a> comes in.</p> \n<p>Before pressing pen to paper (or cursor to digital document), you must understand to whom your branding will be speaking. Who does your product serve? Who is your ideal customer? Why did you create your business in the first place?</p> \n<p>What you learn about your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/target-market\">target market</a> and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buyer-persona-research\">buyer personas</a> will influence your branding decisions down the line, so make this step your first priority.</p> \n<pre class=\"gutter-right\"></pre> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/persona-templates?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase\">Download our free Persona Templates to easily organize your target audience research and strengthen your marketing</a><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/persona-templates\">.</a></em></p> \n<h3>2. Establish your mission statement</h3> \n<p>Let’s return to a question I asked in the previous step: Why did you create your business? Answering this will help you build your mission statement, which defines your purpose and passion as an organization.</p> \n<p>Before you can craft a brand that your audience recognizes, values, and trusts, you must be able to communicate the purpose that your business provides. Then, every part of your brand (logo, tagline, imagery, voice, and personality) can reflect that <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/inspiring-company-mission-statements\">mission and vision</a>.</p> \n<p>Your mission statement is a building block of your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/brand-manifesto\">brand manifesto</a>, which encompasses why your organization exists and why people should care about your brand.</p> \n<p><em>Download our free guide to <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/define-mission-and-vision-statements?hubs_post-cta=pillar_kwphrase\">Defining Inspiring Mission and Vision Statements</a> and learn the ins-and-outs of two of the most valuable strategic planning elements for businesses.</em></p> \n<h3>3. Define your unique values, qualities, and benefits</h3> \n<p>There are probably lots of businesses in your industry and niche. It’s easy to focus on your competition (and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/competitor-analysis-guide\">there’s a time and place for competitive analysis</a>), but, for now, let’s focus on you.</p> \n<p>What’s one thing that your business has that no one else can mimic (er, legally)? <strong>Your brand.</strong></p> \n<p>Because of that, you must ensure that your brand is comprised of and inspired by elements that are solely yours: the values, benefits, and qualities that make your company unique.</p> \n<p>Take a moment to jot down a list of what <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/agency/positioning-agency-branding\">sets your business apart from others</a>. I’m not talking about product features (like appearance, components, or capabilities); I’m referring to how your products or services improve lives and contribute to success.</p> \n<p><strong>Real-life brand example</strong>: <a href=\"https://www.alaninu.com/\">Alani Nutrition</a></p> \n<p>You’ve probably never heard of Alani Nu; they’re a nutrition company based in my hometown of Louisville, Kentucky. I order their vitamins because 1) <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/alaninutrition/\">they’re proven to work</a>, and 2) I trust and respect the brand (and it’s gorgeous!). On their website, they’ve <a href=\"https://www.alaninu.com/pages/our-difference\">clearly and simply outlined their unique values and benefits</a> as part of their overall brand. Highlighting these makes it easy for customers like me to trust their products and choose them over competitors.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/branding-3.png?width=600&amp;name=branding-3.png\" alt=\"branding-3\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\"><span style=\"font-size: 13px;\"></span></img></p> \n<h3>4. Create your visual assets</h3> \n<p>At this point, you should understand your target audience, your mission statement, and the unique qualities that make up your business.</p> \n<p>If you can say with confidence that you’ve mastered these steps, it’s time to move onto one of the more exciting parts of branding — the visual design. We’re talking about your logo, color palette, typography (fonts), iconography, and other visual components.</p> \n<p>As you create these elements, build a set of brand guidelines (or a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/examples-brand-style-guides\">brand style guide</a>) to govern the composition and use of your visual assets. This will ensure that whoever uses your new branding does so accurately and consistently. <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/style-guide\">Check out HubSpot’s brand guidelines for reference.</a></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/branding-1-1.png?width=600&amp;name=branding-1-1.png\" alt=\"branding-1-1\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\" /></p> \n<p><em>Note</em>: Design can be just as intimidating as it is exciting. Consider hiring a professional with <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/design\">logo and identity design experience</a>&nbsp;or starting with a few <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/design-templates\">helpful design templates</a>.</p> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/create-brand-style-guide?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase\">Take your brand to the next level with this free e-book on creating a brand style guide. Download templates, too!</a></em></p> \n<h3>5. Find your brand voice</h3> \n<p>Next, consider the auditory component of your brand. What would your brand sound like if you had a conversation with it, or if it texted you?</p> \n<p>How you communicate with your target market is also considered part of your branding. You want to define a brand voice that connects and resonates with your audience — otherwise, they probably won’t pay attention. Because of that, don’t hesitate to return to step one to get familiar with to whom you’re speaking.</p> \n<p>From your advertising campaigns and social media captions to your blog posts and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/brand-story\">brand story</a>, ensure your tone is consistent throughout all of your written content. Give your audience a chance to get familiar with your brand and learn to recognize the sound of your voice. Better yet, master a fun, entertaining voice, and your customers will <em>look forward</em> to your social media and email updates.</p> \n<p><strong>Real-life brand example</strong>: <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/integrations/mailchimp\">MailChimp</a></p> \n<p>MailChimp is a great example of a brand that speaks with a clear, consistent tone. When I used their free plan for my small business, I always chuckled when receiving their emails and working in their interface. From its web copy to its email blasts and social media captions, MailChimp has established a brand voice and personality that is personable, fun, and accessible — it can be hard to explain the technical parts of a software product <a href=\"https://mailchimp.com/features/ab-testing/\">(like A/B testing), but MailChimp has mastered that, too</a>.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/branding-4.png?width=600&amp;name=branding-4.png\" alt=\"branding-4\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\"><span style=\"font-size: 13px;\"><em><a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/BnJjDMJFMXT/\">Source</a></em></span></img></p> \n<h3><a></a>6. Put your branding to work</h3> \n<p>Your brand only works if you do. Once you finish designing and creating your new brand (or rebrand) integrate it throughout every inch of your business. Pay extra attention to ensure it’s displayed anywhere your business touches customers. Here are a handful of tips for applying your brand across your organization.</p> \n<h4>Website</h4> \n<p>Splash your logo, color palette, and typography across your website. Don’t use anything but your predefined assets in your brand guidelines. Your website is a major part of your company identity — if it doesn’t reflect your brand, it will only provide a jarring customer experience. Also, be sure that all web copy, calls-to-action, and product descriptions reflect your brand voice.</p> \n<h4>Social media</h4> \n<p>All profile photos, cover art, and branded imagery should reflect your brand. Consider putting your logo as your profile photo — this will make it easier for customers to recognize your business. As with your website, be sure all profile information, posts, and captions reflect your brand voice.</p> \n<h4>Packaging</h4> \n<p>If you have a physical products business, your product is probably the most tangible way that customers interact with your brand. For that reason, your packaging should reflect your new branding — in its design, colors, size, and feel.</p> \n<p><strong>Real-life brand example</strong>: <a href=\"https://www.chobani.com/\">Chobani</a></p> \n<p>I love Chobani yogurt (confession: I’m eating it right now). <a href=\"https://www.underconsideration.com/brandnew/archives/new_logo_identity_and_packaging_for_chobani_done_in_house.php\">Their new branding</a> immediately tells me that they produce <a href=\"https://www.chobani.com/about/\">authentic, healthy</a> Greek yogurt. That’s one of the main reasons I buy Chobani. Recently, I realized that their yogurt packages are made with a very earthy, textured material — an <a href=\"https://www.packworld.com/article/package-design/redesign/chobani-stays-top-staying-front\">intentional decision</a> that supports the overall <em>experience</em> they’ve paired with purchasing and eating the Chobani brand.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/branding-2-1.jpg?width=600&amp;name=branding-2-1.jpg\" alt=\"branding-2-1\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\" /></p> \n<h4>Advertising</h4> \n<p>Because advertisements (digital and print) are often used to establish brand awareness and introduce consumers to your brand, it’s critical that they reflect your branding. In fact, your branding should make the ad creation process easier — with your brand style guide, you already know how your ads should appear and what type of copy to write.</p> \n<h4>Sales and customer service</h4> \n<p>A brand is only as powerful as the people behind it, and if your people aren’t putting your brand to work, it won’t work for you. Moreover, your brand applies to more than your marketing. Inform your sales and customer service folks of your brand guidelines and tell them to use it, especially when they engage directly with customers. Whether they are sharing a branded product demo or answering customer support inquiries, encourage them to use your logo, tagline, imagery, and brand voice.</p> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/essential-guide-to-branding-your-company?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase\">Download our Essential Guide to Branding Your Company to learn everything you need to go from same-old business to must-have brand.</a></em></p> \n<div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet\"> \n <div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet__wrapper\"> \n  <h2><a></a>Branding Tips for Small Business</h2> \n  <ul> \n   <li class=\"hsg-featured-snippet__wrapper--content\">Treat your brand as a person</li> \n   <li class=\"hsg-featured-snippet__wrapper--content\">Prioritize consistency</li> \n   <li class=\"hsg-featured-snippet__wrapper--content\">Follow a brand strategy</li> \n   <li class=\"hsg-featured-snippet__wrapper--content\">Don’t let inspiration turn into imitation</li> \n   <li class=\"hsg-featured-snippet__wrapper--content\">Use branding to hire</li> \n  </ul> \n </div> \n</div> \n<h3>Treat your brand as a person</h3> \n<p>To best wrap your head around the branding process, think of your brand as a person. Your brand should have an identity (who it is), personality (how it behaves), and experience (how it’s remembered).</p> \n<p>Ask yourself these questions about your brand:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>How would your brand introduce itself? If it had to describe its appearance, how would it do so?</li> \n <li>How would your brand talk about your products or services? Would it be serious and professional, or would it be humorous and edgy?</li> \n <li>What would someone say about your brand after “meeting” it for the first time? What are a few sentences they’d use to describe it?</li> \n</ul> \n<p>The purpose of branding is to create relationships with your customers. The easiest way to do this is to treat your brand as a person and understand that you want your customers to do the same.</p> \n<p><strong>Real-life brand example</strong>: <a href=\"https://www.whiskeyriff.com/\">Whiskey Riff</a></p> \n<p>Whiskey Riff is another brand you’re probably not familiar with. It’s a two-man media company based here in Chicago that’s dubbed themselves “the most entertaining country music site ever”. I’m a fan because I love country music, enjoy their written and podcast content, and proudly wear some of <a href=\"https://shop.whiskeyriff.com/\">their awesome apparel</a>.</p> \n<p>If Whiskey Riff was a person, here’s how I’d think it would answer the questions above:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>“Hey, I’m Whiskey Riff. I love country music and, you guessed it, Whiskey. My logo was inspired by the<span><span>&nbsp;</span><a href=\"http://www.publicartinchicago.com/chicago-the-y-symbol-municipal-device/\">Y in the circle on the Chicago Theater marquee</a>, and I'm&nbsp;</span>adorned with horizontal red stripes and stars —&nbsp;which&nbsp;represent&nbsp;the American and Chicago flags.”</li> \n <li>“I publish in-your-face content about what’s going on in country music today. If you don’t like it, don’t read it. My podcast featured my founders interviewing country music artists and telling hilarious stories. Check out my apparel line; my t-shirts, tanks, hats, and accessories can be seen at country music festivals (and on stages) nationwide.”</li> \n <li>“Whiskey Riff is like that first shot of Jack Daniels — that much-needed, refreshing drink after a long day. Its a break from that cookie-cutter way of life, and you immediately appreciate — and trust — its candidness. There’s absolutely nothing like it in the industry.”</li> \n</ul> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/branding-5.png?width=600&amp;name=branding-5.png\" alt=\"branding-5\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\" /></p> \n<h3>Prioritize consistency</h3> \n<p>Inconsistency is <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/branding-mistakes\">the number one branding mistake</a> that companies make. Inconsistency undermines your brand and confuses your customers. Recognizable, valuable brands prioritize consistency — and they reap the benefits. When your brand is a unified presence across mediums and platforms, customers can easily get familiar with, recognize, and come to prefer your brand over time. Brand guidelines can help with this initiative.</p> \n<h3>Build and follow a brand strategy</h3> \n<p>A <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/31739/7-components-that-comprise-a-comprehensive-brand-strategy.aspx\">brand strategy</a> is more than your brand guidelines; it’s a plan with specific, long-term goals that can be achieved as your brand evolves. These goals typically revolve around your brand’s purpose, emotion, flexibility, competitive awareness, and employee involvement.</p> \n<p>Remember how I said that branding is a continuous process? There’s a lot that goes into it. A brand strategy can help you turn that process into a well-oiled practice that keeps your brand moving toward success and recognition.</p> \n<h3>Don’t let inspiration turn into imitation</h3> \n<p>Competitive analysis is important. Not only does it educate you on where your competition stands and how they are excelling, but it can also give you ideas on how you can improve or further set apart your brand.</p> \n<p>However, be conscious to not fall into an imitation trap. Keep your competitive research limited and focus on what your organization brings to the table. Just because a competitor (or two) has branded their company in a certain way doesn’t mean that you have to follow suit. New, unique, provocative brands are memorable brands.</p> \n<h3>Use branding to hire</h3> \n<p>Strong branding makes your employees proud. I know I’m proud to be associated with HubSpot, much less <em>work</em> there. Leverage your branding to attract talented people. If hiring is a strong initiative for your organization, dedicate some of your resources to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/employer-branding\">employer branding</a>. Employer branding is how you market your company to job seekers and current employees. If you’re publically proud of your organization, others will be, too.</p> \n<h2>Ready, Set, Brand</h2> \n<p>Branding is your organization’s name, logo, color palette, voice, and imagery. It’s also more. It’s that <em>intangible</em> feeling your customers have when they interact with your brand. You know … that <em>experience</em> we talked about in the beginning.</p> \n<p>That’s how powerhouse brands deviate from all the others. The tangible components contribute to this — a gorgeous logo, a clever tagline, an authentic manifesto, and a clear brand voice — but truly strong brands thrive when they focus on the big picture of their brand. Get to the heart and soul of your target audience <em>and</em> your organization, and a successful brand will follow.&nbsp;</p> \n<p></p> \n<p></p> \n<img 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"Brand Strategy 101: 7 Essentials for Strong Company Branding","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/31739/7-components-that-comprise-a-comprehensive-brand-strategy.aspx","description":"<p>Let's say you've come to the difficult realization that quite frankly your brand -- if you can even call it that -- is <strong style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\"><em>all over</em></strong> the place. Or perhaps worse, you have a defined brand, but you're noticing that it just doesn't seem to mesh with who you <em style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">really</em> are and what you <em style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">really</em> do.</p> \n<p>Don't panic.</p> \n<p>Before you get all hung up on what shade of green to use for your logo or what tone you're going to use when engaging with people on Twitter, you need to step back and take a look at the big picture.</p> \n<h3>What is Brand Strategy?</h3> \n<p>Brand strategy is a plan that encompasses specific, long-term goals that can be achieved with the evolution of a successful brand -- the combined components of your company's character that make it identifiable.</p> \n<p>(We'll get into that more in a bit.)</p> \n<p>A well-defined and executed brand strategy affects all aspects of a business and is directly connected to consumer needs, emotions, and competitive environments.</p> \n<p>First, let's clear up the biggest misconception about brand strategy: Your brand is not your product, your logo, your website, or your name.</p> \n<p>In fact, your brand is much more than that -- it's the stuff that feels intangible. But it's that hard-to-pin-down feeling that separates powerhouse and mediocre brands from each other.</p> \n<p>So to help you rein in what many marketers consider more of an art and less of a science, we've broken down seven essential components of a comprehensive brand strategy that will help keep your company around for ages.</p> \n<div class=\"video-container-responsive\">\n <iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/z25lC85v9Zw\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div> \n<h2>7 Components for a Comprehensive Branding Strategy</h2> \n<h3>1) Purpose</h3> \n<p>\"Every brand makes a promise. But in a marketplace in which consumer confidence is low and budgetary vigilance is high, it’s not just making a promise that separates one brand from another, but having a defining purpose,\" <a href=\"http://www.forbes.com/2009/11/11/brand-defining-marketing-cmo-network-allen-adamson.html\">explains Allen Adamson</a>, chairman of the North America region of brand consulting and design firm Landor Associates.</p> \n<p>While understanding what your business promises is necessary when defining your brand positioning, knowing <em>why</em> you wake up every day and go to work carries more weight. In other words, your purpose is more specific, in that it serves as a differentiator between you and your competitors.</p> \n<p>How can you define your business' purpose? According to <a href=\"http://www.brandingstrategyinsider.com/2014/08/defining-your-brand-purpose.html#.VcTD11PF-vo\">Business Strategy Insider</a>, purpose can be viewed in two ways:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Functional: </strong>This concept focuses on the evaluations of success in terms of immediate and commercial reasons -- i.e. the purpose of the business is to make money.</li> \n <li><strong>Intentional: </strong>This concept focuses on success as it relates to the ability to make money and do good in the world.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>While making money is important to almost every business, we admire brands that emphasize their willingness to achieve more than just profitability, like IKEA:</p> \n<p><img class=\"wt-blog__normal-image\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/00-Blog-Related_Images/IKEA_Vision.png?width=508&amp;height=322&amp;name=IKEA_Vision.png\" width=\"508\" height=\"322\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\">Source:<em> <a href=\"http://www.ikea.com/ms/en_SG/about_ikea/our_business_idea/index.html\">IKEA</a></em></span></p> \n<p>IKEA's vision isn't just to sell furniture, but rather, to \"create a better everyday life.\" This approach is appealing to potential customers, as it demonstrates their commitment to providing value beyond the point of sale.</p> \n<p>When defining your business' purpose, keep this example in mind. While making money is a priority, operating under that notion alone does little to set your brand apart from others in your industry.</p> \n<p>Our advice? Dig a little deeper. If you need inspiration, check out the brands you admire, and see how they frame their mission and vision statements.</p> \n<h3>2) Consistency</h3> \n<p>The key to consistency is to avoid talking about things that don’t relate to or enhance your brand. Added a new photo to your business' <a title=\"Facebook\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/Beyond-the-Facebook-Business-Page/\">Facebook Page</a>? What does it mean for your company? Does it align with your message, or was it just something funny that would, quite frankly, confuse your audience?</p> \n<p>In an effort to give your brand a platform to stand on, you need to be sure that all of your messaging is cohesive. Ultimately, consistency contributes to brand recognition, which fuels customer loyalty. (No pressure, right?)</p> \n<p>To see a great example of consistency, let's look at <a href=\"http://us.coca-cola.com/home/\">Coca-Cola</a>. As a result of its commitment to consistency, every element of the brand's marketing works harmoniously together. This has helped it become one of the most <a href=\"http://www.forbes.com/powerful-brands/\">recognizable brands in the world</a>.</p> \n<p>Even on the surface of its social media accounts, for example, the seamlessness of its brand is very apparent:</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.52.07%20PM.png?width=600&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.52.07%20PM.png\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.54.07%20PM.png?width=600&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.54.07%20PM.png\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.55.35%20PM.png?width=600&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.55.35%20PM.png\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.57.02%20PM.png?width=600&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.57.02%20PM.png\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px;\"></p> \n<p>To avoid leaving potential customers struggling to put the disconnected pieces of your business together, consider the benefits of creating a style guide. A style guide can encompass everything from the tone of voice you'll use to the color scheme you'll employ to the way you'll position certain products or services.</p> \n<p>By taking the time to define and agree upon these considerations, your brand will benefit as a whole.</p> \n<h3>3) Emotion</h3> \n<p>Customers aren't always rational.</p> \n<p>How else do you explain the person who paid thousands of dollars more for a Harley rather than buying another cheaper, equally well-made bike? There was an emotional voice in there somewhere, whispering: <em>“Buy a Harley.” </em></p> \n<p>But why?</p> \n<p><a href=\"http://www.harley-davidson.com/content/h-d/en_US/home.html\">Harley Davidson</a> uses emotional branding by creating a community around its brand. It began <a href=\"https://members.hog.com/website/index.jsp?redirectUrl=https%3A%2F%2Fmembers.hog.com%2Fwebsite%2Fmain.jsp%3Fhbx_camp_id%3Dhdredirect%26amp%3Burlvar%3Dhogcom%26amp%3Bcamp_id%3D16%26amp%3Bsource_cd%3DVanity_hogcom\">HOG</a> -- Harley Owners Group -- to connect their customers with their brand (and each other).</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.59.16%20PM.png?width=600&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202017-10-05%20at%203.59.16%20PM.png\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\">Source:<em> <a href=\"https://members.hog.com/website/index.jsp?redirectUrl=https%3A%2F%2Fmembers.hog.com%2Fwebsite%2Fmain.jsp%3Fhbx_camp_id%3Dhdredirect%26amp%3Burlvar%3Dhogcom%26amp%3Bcamp_id%3D16%26amp%3Bsource_cd%3DVanity_hogcom\">HOG</a></em></span></p> \n<p>By providing customers with an opportunity to feel like they're part of a larger group that's more tight-knit than just a bunch of motorcycle riders, Harley Davidson is able to position themselves as an obvious choice for someone looking to purchase a bike.</p> \n<p>Why? People have an innate desire to build relationships. Research from psychologists Roy Baumeister and Mark Leary best describes this need in their \"<a href=\"http://www.scienceofrelationships.com/home/2012/4/16/the-need-to-belong-part-of-what-makes-us-human.html\">belongingness hypothesis</a>,\" which states: \"People have a basic psychological need to feel closely connected to others, and that caring, affectionate bonds from close relationships are a major part of human behavior.\"</p> \n<p>Not to mention, belongingness -- the need for love, affection, and being part of groups -- falls directly in the middle of Maslow's hierarchy of needs, which aims to categorize different human needs.</p> \n<p>The lesson to be learned? Find a way to connect with your customers on a deeper, more emotional level. Do you give them peace of mind? Make them feel like part of the family? Do you make life easier? Use emotional triggers like these to strengthen your relationship and foster loyalty.</p> \n<h3>4) Flexibility</h3> \n<p>In this fast-changing world, marketers must remain flexible to stay relevant. On the plus side, this frees you to be creative with your campaigns.</p> \n<p>You may be thinking, <em>\"Wait a minute, how am I supposed to remain consistent while also being flexible?\"</em></p> \n<p>Good question. While consistency aims to set the standard for your brand, flexibility enables you to make adjustments that build interest and distinguish your approach from that of your competition.</p> \n<p>In other words, \"effective identity programs require enough consistency to be identifiable, but enough variation to keep things fresh and human,\" <a href=\"http://www.peopledesign.com/brand-variation\">explains </a><a href=\"http://www.peopledesign.com/brand-variation\">president of Peopledesign</a>, Kevin Budelmann.</p> \n<p>A great example of this type of strategic balance comes from <a href=\"http://oldspice.com/en\">Old Spice</a>. These days, Old Spice is one of the best examples of successful marketing across the board. However, up until recently, wearing Old Spice was pretty much an unspoken requirement for dads everywhere. Today, it's one of the most popular brands for men of all ages.</p> \n<p>The secret? Flexibility.</p> \n<p>Aware that it needed to do something to secure its place in the market, <a href=\"https://www.wk.com/office/portland/client/old_spice\">Old Spice teamed up with Wieden+Kennedy</a> to position their brand for a new customer base.</p> \n<p><img class=\"wt-blog__normal-image\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Old_Spice_Before_and_After.png?width=560&amp;height=328&amp;name=Old_Spice_Before_and_After.png\" width=\"560\" height=\"328\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></p> \n<span style=\"font-size: 12px;\">Source:<em> <a href=\"http://worksdesigngroup.com/brand-stories-old-spice-rebrand/\">Works Design Group</a></em></span> \n<p>Between new commercials, a new website, new packaging, and new product names, Old Spice managed to attract the attention of a new, younger generation by making strategic enhancements to its already strong brand.</p> \n<p>So if your old tactics aren’t working anymore, don’t be afraid to change. Just because it worked in the past doesn't mean it's working now.</p> \n<p>Take the opportunity to engage your followers in fresh, new ways. Are there some out-of-the-box partnerships your brand can make? Are there attributes about your product you never highlighted? Use those to connect with new customers and remind your old ones why they love you.</p> \n<h3>5) Employee Involvement</h3> As we mentioned before, achieving a sense of consistency is important if you wish to build brand recognition. And while a style guide can help you achieve a cohesive digital experience, it's equally important for your employees to be well versed in the how they should be communicating with customers and representing the brand. \n<p>If your brand is playful and bubbly through Twitter engagements, then it wouldn't make sense if a customer called in and was connected with a grumpy, monotone representative, right?</p> \n<p>To avoid this type of mismatched experience, take note of Zappos' approach.</p> \n<p>If you've ever been on the line with a customer service representative from Zappos, you know what I'm talking about. If you haven't, <a href=\"http://www.slideshare.net/InfinitOInc/10-inspiring-zappos-customer-support-stories\">check out this SlideShare</a> which details some of its most inspiring customer support stories.</p> \n<p><a href=\"http://www.zappos.com/\">Zappos</a> is so committed to ensuring that not only its&nbsp;brand, <em>but all brands,</em> remain consistent across digital and human interactions that they've dedicated an entire department to the cause called <a href=\"http://www.zapposinsights.com/\">Zappos Insights.</a></p>  \n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\"> \n <p>Come join us and learn the Zappos WOW approach to customer service! Learn more about the Zappos School of WOW: <a href=\"https://t.co/g3tU4179q9\">https://t.co/g3tU4179q9</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/eRkpcfYAKD\">pic.twitter.com/eRkpcfYAKD</a></p> — Zappos Insights (@ZapposInsights) \n <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ZapposInsights/status/899755090915020801?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 21, 2017</a>\n</blockquote>  By holding all Zappos employees to its core values \n<em>and</em> helping other companies implement the same approach, Zappos has built a strong reputation for solid, helpful, and human customer service.\n<br> \n<h3>6) Loyalty</h3> \n<p>If you already have people that love you, your company, and your brand, don’t just sit there. Reward them for that love.</p> \n<p>These customers have gone out their way to write about you, to tell their friends about you, and to act as your brand ambassadors. Cultivating loyalty from these people early on will yield more returning customers -- and more profit for your business.</p> \n<p>Sometimes, just a thank you is all that's needed. Other times, it's better to go above and beyond. Write them a personalized letter. Sent them some special swag. Ask them to write a review, and feature them prominently on your website. (Or all of the above!)</p> \n<p>When we reached <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/15k\">15,000 customers here at HubSpot</a>, we wanted to say thank you in a big way, while remaining true to our brand ... so we dropped 15,000 orange ping pong balls from our fourth-floor balcony and spelled out thank you in big metallic balloons:</p> \n<div class=\"video-container-responsive\">\n <iframe style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/_Nints9uh4o\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div> \n<p>And while it may have seemed a little out of the ordinary to some folks, for those who know our brand, the gesture made perfect sense.</p> \n<p>Loyalty is a critical part of every brand strategy, especially if you're looking to support your sales organization. At the end of the day, highlighting a positive relationship between you and your existing customers sets the tone for what potential customers can expect if they choose to do business with you.</p> \n<h3>7) Competitive Awareness</h3> \n<p>Take the competition as a challenge to improve your own strategy and create greater value in your overall brand. You are in the same business and going after the same customers, right? So watch what they do.</p> \n<p>Do some of their tactics succeed? Do some fail? Tailor your brand positioning based on their experience to better your company.</p> \n<p>A great example of how to improve your brand by learning from your competitors comes from <a href=\"https://twitter.com/pizzahut\">Pizza Hut</a>:</p> \n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\"> \n <p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/TherealElysium?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@TheRealElysium</a> You know our vote. ^AB</p> — Pizza Hut (@pizzahut) \n <a href=\"https://twitter.com/pizzahut/status/711617215649349632?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 20, 2016</a>\n</blockquote> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\">  </p> \n<p>When a pizza lover posed this question to his Twitter following, Pizza Hut didn't miss a beat, and playfully responded in minutes, before <a href=\"https://twitter.com/dominos\">Domino's</a> had a chance to speak up.</p> \n<p>If Domino's is keeping an eye on the competitors, they'll know to act fast the next time a situation like this arises.</p> \n<p>For HubSpot customers, keeping tabs on your competitor's social mentions is easy using the <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/social-inbox\">Social Monitoring App</a>. <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/social-media-user-guide/how-to-create-streams-in-the-social-monitoring-tool\">Check out this article</a> to learn more about how to set up custom social streams.</p> \n<p>And while staying in tune with your competitor's strategies is important if you want to enhance your brand, don't let them dictate each and every move you make.</p> \n<p>Sure, you probably sell a similar product or service as many other companies, but you're in business because your brand is unique. By harping on every move your competitor makes, you lose that differentiation.</p> \n<p></p> \n<div>\n <a class=\"close\">&nbsp;</a>\n</div>  \n<img
