My whole world was shattered. Granted, I was about eight, but I was furious to find out that <em>my </em><em>parents </em>had been putting a quarter under my pillow every time I'd lost a tooth, not a sweet fairy named Daphne who lived in a castle made out of my pearly whites.</p> \n<p>Luckily, believing in the Tooth Fairy is pretty harmless. Other myths, especially those that affect your business, are not.</p> \n<p>In previous posts, we've debunked myths about <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/insiders/marketing-automation-facts\">marketing automation</a>, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33734/20-Common-Social-Media-Marketing-Myths-BUSTED.aspx\">social media</a>, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blogging-myths-ht\">blogging</a>, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33926/7-Common-SEO-Myths-to-Throw-Out-the-Window-Immediately.aspx\">SEO</a>, and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34254/11-Common-A-B-Testing-Myths-BUSTED.aspx\">A/B testing</a>... but we've never touched on <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-landing-page-builder\">landing pages</a>.</p> \n<p>Keep reading so you don't miss out on information that'll help you convert visitors into leads and leads into customers. We'll debunk the most common landing page myths and arm you with information to take your landing pages to the next level.</p> \n<p></p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #1: You only need a few of them.</strong></h2> \n<p>Lots of people think that you don't need many landing pages. Maybe you have a 'Contact Us' page and a demo page, and that's pretty much it, right? Wrong. If you only have a few landing pages, you're missing out on traffic, leads, and customers <em>big time.</em></p> \n<p>Every new landing page you create is another opportunity for you to appear in search engines and get your link shared on social media -- and better search engine rankings and social media posts mean that you'll have more opportunity to drive traffic and conversions for your website.</p> \n<p>Additionally, besides landing pages on your website, you're going to need landing pages to convert leads. These pages are probably not available on search engines, but will help you track how many leads have clicked into an offer and how many have downloaded your content offers.</p> \n<p>Need more convincing about the importance of having more landing pages? <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33756/Why-You-Yes-You-Need-to-Create-More-Landing-Pages.aspx\">Check out this post.</a></p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #2:</strong><strong>Short forms are better than long forms.</strong></h2> \n<p>No <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/forms\">form</a> length is the \"best\" -- it all depends on what you're trying to accomplish with the form. Are you trying to get a ton of new leads? Keep the form short. Are you trying to get really qualified leads? Make the form longer. One is not better than the other -- they just address different goals.</p> \n<p>Your form length will most likely end up somewhere in the middle. To find <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/32079/How-Long-Should-Your-Landing-Page-Forms-Be.aspx\">your form length sweet spot</a>, run A/B tests and adjust your form length according to their results.</p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #3:</strong><strong>If I copy someone else's landing page, my conversion rates will go up.</strong></h2> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/landing-page-examples-list\">Landing page examples</a> and templates are great jumping off points for your own landing pages, but you shouldn't expect to plug your content into someone else's landing page and end up raking in the conversions. A landing page is successful because of interaction of many nuanced elements -- the content on the page, the design of the page, and the audience viewing the page.</p> \n<p>If you're going to copy a landing page layout, use best practices to <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/conversion-centered-design\">tweak it to help</a> <em>your</em> audience convert on <em>your</em> offer, then test it and test it to make it better.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, a landing page will only succeed if the content offer matches the intent of the customer.</p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #4:</strong><strong>You need to have all conversion elements above the fold.</strong></h2> \n<p>Lots of people believe that all of the important content on your landing page should appear above the fold -- supposedly, people won't scroll to fill out the form or find out more crucial information about what lies behind the form.</p> \n<p>But the fold doesn't really affect conversion -- <a href=\"https://blog.kissmetrics.com/why-the-fold-is-a-myth/\">KISSmetrics found</a> that when people are motivated to convert on a page, they do, regardless of where the form submit button is. According to that article, the biggest factor in increasing motivation is compelling copy, regardless of length. So forget optimizing <em>only</em> for the fold -- through A/B testing, figure out how much information people need to convert.</p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #5: Trust seals always increase conversions.</strong></h2> \n<p>Think about the situations in which you often see trust seals. You're usually giving over your credit card number or some other sensitive contact information, right? It makes sense to get a little visual reminder that your information is safe, because you really are giving over sensitive information.</p> \n<p>But what if you saw a trust seal on a page where you <em>weren't </em>giving over sensitive information? It'd be out-of-place, making you wonder what the heck the company was really collecting from you, right? Trust elements can help tremendously on pages that need them -- but they can also deter folks if they're included on pages that don't.</p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #6: If you change your form button from green to red, you'll increase conversions.</strong></h2> \n<p>Full disclosure: <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/20566/The-Button-Color-A-B-Test-Red-Beats-Green.aspx\">we've run this test</a> and found that a red call-to-action (CTA) outperformed a green CTA ... but that doesn't mean that red buttons are <em>always</em> better than green ones. That test worked for that page, with that page's design, for that page's audience. If you run the same test on your site, you might find that the opposite is true.</p> \n<p>This myth goes for any color test really --<strong>there is no one <em>right</em> color that'll convert tons and tons more people</strong>. Test out colors yourself to see what works best.</p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #7: Landing page copy should <em>always</em> be short and sweet.</strong></h2> \n<p>Like color, there's no right length of landing page copy. We kind of touched on this in Myth #4, but the copy length myth is perpetuated enough it deserved a section of its own.</p> \n<p>Landing page copy length is like what your teachers would say when you'd ask them how long an essay should be -- however long it needs to be to cover the subject. In the case of landing pages, it should be however long you need it to be to have people convert on your landing page's form. For complex offers that require people ponying up a lot of money or their sensitive information, more information could be better. For simple offers, like an ebook, you probably don't need a ton of landing page copy.</p> \n<p>Like almost all of these myths, this one's nuanced. Run tests on your landing pages to find out what copy length your visitors need.</p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #8: Conversion rate is the only metric to watch.</strong></h2> \n<p>Landing pages are a stepping stone in your marketing funnel. You're not just trying to get people to fill out a form. You'd hope that eventually they'll become a customer from you.</p> \n<p>So if you're trying to get the most out of your landing pages, you shouldn't just look at the percent of people who converted on that form -- you want to look and see what happens after.</p> \n<p>What percentage of them become customers? By looking at your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/definition-closed-loop-analytics-under-100-words-sr\">closed-loop analytics</a>, you may find that a landing page that has a low initial conversion rate actually brings in customers like crazy, or vice versa ... which is something your boss would care to know and fix.</p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #9: You should include as many things as possible on your landing page to get people to convert on <em>something</em>.</strong></h2> \n<p>Your landing page isn't a last-ditch effort to capture someone's information. It's there to get people to convert on your form and move down your marketing funnel. You don't want to give people too many options because they'll get distracted and your conversion rate goes down. This means you should <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/landing-page-navigation-ht\">try removing your navigation </a>and any extraneous forms. More is not better when it comes to landing page elements.</p> \n<h2><strong>Myth #10: You build 'em and leave 'em.</strong></h2> \n<p>You could probably guess this last myth from one piece of advice I've repeated over and over throughout this post: Test your landing pages. There are almost always ways you can tweak and improve them. If you build them and leave them alone, you're losing out on valuable conversions. Landing pages support the backbone of your marketing funnel -- so make sure you're getting the most you can out of them by running A/B tests often.</p> \n<p>Building a landing page can feel like a daunting task with the contradictory advice out there. That's why you should use a <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/landing-pages\">landing page builder</a> to assist you.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in March 2014 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p><em></em></p> \n<p><em></em></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Flanding-page-myths-list&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 13 Nov 2020 12:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"a4f91e6fc23bf48ad60bfbc8f54c6f1d","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"gsoskey@hubspot.com (Ginny Mineo)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Flanding-page-myths-list&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn6@2020_6/2020/11/14/17-30-25-101_bffbcbd64f5d4549.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605375018181},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"YouTube SEO: How to Optimize Videos for YouTube Search","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/youtube-seo","description":"<p>As recently as a decade ago, inbound marketing was a brand new idea. Marketers were learning that they couldn't just publish a high volume of content -- it also had to be high-quality and optimized in ways that made it as discoverable as possible through search engines.</p> \n<p>That content was once largely limited to the written word. Today, that's no longer the case.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>Today, a comprehensive content strategy includes written work like blogs and ebooks, <em>as well as</em> media like podcasts, visual assets, and videos.</p> \n<p>That last part -- video -- continues to be on the rise. According to the 2018 <a href=\"http://stateofinbound.com/\">State of Inbound</a> report, 45% of marketers are investing more in YouTube over the course of this year -- more than any other marketing channel available to them.</p> \n<p>And with the rise of other content formats comes the need to optimize them for search. One increasingly important place to do that is on YouTube, a video distribution website used by the masses -- HubSpot included.</p> \n<div class=\"hs-embed-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; width: 100%; height: auto; padding: 0px; max-width: 560px; max-height: 315px; min-width: 256px; display: block; margin: auto;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-embed-content-wrapper\"> \n  <div style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.25%; margin: 0px;\"> \n   <iframe width=\"480\" height=\"270\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/pNnMBwS4Bdc?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\"></iframe> \n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<p>But how does YouTube SEO work? What are the steps you need to take to optimize your YouTube channel for search? We've outlined some major tips and tools below.</p> \n<p class=\"p1\"></p> \n<div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet\"> \n <h2>YouTube SEO Tips</h2> \n <ol> \n  <li>Rename your video file using a target keyword.</li> \n  <li>Insert your keyword naturally in the video title.</li> \n  <li>Optimize your video description.</li> \n  <li>Tag your video with popular keywords that relate to your topic.</li> \n  <li>Categorize your video.</li> \n  <li>Upload a custom thumbnail image for your video's result link.</li> \n  <li>Use an SRT file to add subtitles &amp; closed captions.</li> \n  <li>Add Cards and End Screens to increase your YouTube channel's viewership.</li> \n </ol> \n</div> \n<h3>1. Rename your video file using a target keyword.</h3> \n<p>Just like you would when optimizing written content, you'll use an SEO tool to first identify keywords you'd like your video to focus on (you can browse popular <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/youtube-seo#tools\">YouTube SEO tools</a> below these tips, or just click that link earlier in this sentence).</p> \n<p>With a keyword identified, the first place you should put it is your video file -- before you even upload it to YouTube. Why? YouTube can't actually \"watch\" your video to see how relevant it is to your target keyword, and as you'll learn in the tips below, there are only so many places you can safely insert this keyword on your video's viewing page once it's published. But, YouTube <em>can</em> read your video's file name and all the code that comes with it when it's uploaded.</p> \n<p>With that in mind, replace the \"business_ad_003FINAL.mov\" file name (don't be embarrassed ... we've all been there during post-production) with your desired keyword. If your keyword is \"house painting tips,\" for example, your video's file name should be \"house-painting-tips\" followed by your preferred video file type (MOV, MP4, and WMV are some of the most common that are compatible with YouTube).</p> \n<h3>2. Insert your keyword naturally in the video title.</h3> \n<p>When we search for videos, one of the first things that our eyes are drawn to is the title. That's often what determines whether or not the viewer will click to watch your video, so the title should not only be compelling, but also clear and concise.</p> \n<p>Although your keyword plays a big part in your video title, it also helps if the title closely matches what the viewer is searching for. Research conducted by Backlinko found that videos with an exact keyword match in the title have only a slight advantage over those that don't. Here's a linear representation of those findings:</p> \n<img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/exact-match-title.png?width=669&amp;name=exact-match-title.png\" alt=\"exact-match-title.png\" width=\"669\" title=\"exact-match-title.png\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> <span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><em>Source: <a href=\"http://backlinko.com/youtube-ranking-factors\">Backlinko</a></em></span> <p>So, while \"using your target keyword in your title may help you rank for that term,\" report author <a href=\"http://backlinko.com/youtube-ranking-factors\">Brian Dean</a> explains, \"the relationship between keyword-rich video titles and rankings\" isn't always a strong one. Nonetheless, it's a good idea to optimize your title for this keyword so long as it fits naturally into a title that tells viewers exactly what they're about to see.</p> <p>Lastly, make sure to keep your title fairly short -- HubSpot campaigns manager <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/aliciacollins/\">Alicia Collins</a> recommends limiting it to 60 characters to help keep it from getting cut off in results pages.</p> <h3>3. Optimize your video description.</h3> <p>First things first: According to <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/3027950?hl=en\">Google</a>, the official character limit for YouTube video descriptions is 1,000 characters. And while it's okay to use all of that space, remember that your viewer most likely came here to watch a video, not to read an essay.</p> <p>If you do choose to write a longer description, keep in mind that YouTube only displays the first two or three lines of text -- that amounts to about 100 characters. After that point, viewers have to click \"show more\" to see the full description. That's why we suggest front-loading the description with the most important information, like CTAs or crucial links.</p> <p>As for optimizing the video itself, it doesn't hurt to add a transcript of the video, especially for those who have to watch it without volume. That said, Backlinko's research also found no <a href=\"http://backlinko.com/youtube-ranking-factors\">correlation between descriptions that were optimized for a certain keyword and the rankings for that term</a>.</p> <img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/keyword-in-description.png?width=669&amp;name=keyword-in-description.png\" alt=\"keyword-in-description.png\" width=\"669\" title=\"keyword-in-description.png\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> <span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><em>Source: <a href=\"http://backlinko.com/youtube-ranking-factors\">Backlinko</a></em></span> <p>Dean is careful <em>not</em> to encourage ditching an optimized description altogether, though. \"An optimized description helps you show up in the suggested videos sidebar,\" he writes, \"which is a significant source of views for most channels.\"</p> <h3>4. Tag your video with popular keywords that relate to your topic.</h3> <p>YouTube's official <a href=\"https://creatoracademy.youtube.com/page/lesson/discovery#yt-creators-strategies-2\">Creator Academy</a> suggests using tags to let viewers know what your video is about. But you're not just informing your viewers -- you're also informing YouTube itself. Dean explains that the platform uses tags \"to understand the content and context of your video.\"</p> <p>That way, YouTube figures out how to associate your video with similar videos, which can broaden your content's reach. But choose your tags wisely. Don't use an irrelevant tag because you think it'll get you more views -- in fact, Google might <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/7002331?hl=en&amp;ref_topic=4355198\">penalize</a> you for that. And similar to your description, lead with the most important keywords, including a good mix of those that are common and more long-tail (as in, those that answer a question like \"how do I?\").</p> <h3>5. Categorize your video.</h3> <p>Once you upload a video, you can categorize it under \"Advanced settings.\" Choosing a category is another way to group your video with similar content on YouTube so it winds up in different playlists and gains exposure to more viewers who identify with your audience.</p> <p>It might not be as simple as it looks. In fact, YouTube's <a href=\"https://creatoracademy.youtube.com/page/lesson/overview-categories?cid=platform&amp;hl=en#yt-creators-strategies-2\">Creator Academy</a> suggests marketers go through a comprehensive process to determine which category each video belongs in. It's helpful, the guide writes, \"to think about what is working well for each category\" you're considering by answering questions like:</p> \n  <ul> \n   <li>Who are the top creators within the category? What are they known for and what do they do well?</li> \n   <li>Are there any patterns between the audiences of similar channels within a given category?</li> \n   <li>Do the videos within a similar category have share qualities like production value, length, or format?</li> \n  </ul> <h3>6. Upload a custom thumbnail image for your video's result link.</h3> <p>Your video thumbnail is the main image viewers see when scrolling through a list of video results. Along with the video's title, that thumbnail sends a signal to the viewer about the video's content, so it can impact the number of clicks and views your video receives.</p> <p>While you can always pick one of the thumbnail options auto-generated by YouTube, we highly recommend uploading a custom thumbnail. The Creator Academy reports that \"<a href=\"https://creatoracademy.youtube.com/page/lesson/thumbnails#yt-creators-strategies-1\">90% of the best performing videos on YouTube have custom thumbnails</a>,\" recommending the use of images that are 1280x720 pixels -- representing a 16:9 ratio -- that are saved as 2MB or smaller .jpg, .gif, .bmp, or .png files. If you follow those parameters, it can help to ensure that your thumbnail appears with equally high quality across multiple viewing platforms.</p> <p>It's important to note that your YouTube account has to be <em>verified</em> in order to upload a custom thumbnail image. To do that, visit <a href=\"http://youtube.com/verify\">youtube.com/verify</a> and follow the instructions listed there.</p> <h3>7. Use an SRT File to add subtitles &amp; closed captions.</h3> <p>Like much of the other text we've discussed here, subtitles and closed captions can boost YouTube search optimization by highlighting important keywords.</p> <p>In order to add subtitles or closed captions to your video, you'll have to upload a supported text transcript or timed subtitles file. For the former, you can also directly enter transcript text for a video so that it auto-syncs with the video.</p> <p>Adding subtitles follows a similar process, however, you can limit the amount of text you want displayed. For either, head to your video manager then click on \"Videos\" under \"Video Manager.\" Find the video you want to add subtitles or closed captioning to, and click the drop-down arrow next to the edit button. Then, choose \"Subtitles/CC.\" You can then select how you'd like to add subtitles or closed captioning.</p> <p>Find out how to add closed captions to your YouTube video in the video below.</p> \n  <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"width: 100%; height: auto; position: relative; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; min-width: 256px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; margin: 0px auto;\"> \n   <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 59.38%; margin: 0;\"> \n    <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe hs-fullwidth-embed\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/h-HlBPx8ek4\" width=\"640\" height=\"380\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n   </div> \n  </div> <h3>8. Add Cards and End Screens to increase your YouTube channel's viewership.</h3> <h4 class=\"p1\">Cards</h4> <p>When you're watching a video, have you ever seen a small white, circular icon with an \"i\" in the center appear in the corner, or a translucent bar of text asking you to subscribe? Those are Cards, which <a href=\"https://creatoracademy.youtube.com/page/lesson/cards?cid=get-discovered&amp;hl=en#yt-creators-strategies-1\">Creator Academy</a> describes as \"preformatted notifications that appear on desktop and mobile which you can set up to promote your brand and other videos on your channel.\"</p> <img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202017-05-25%20at%206.02.40%20PM.png?width=641&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202017-05-25%20at%206.02.40%20PM.png\" alt=\"&quot;i&quot; icon to create End Cards in YouTube video \" width=\"641\" title=\"Screen Shot 2017-05-25 at 6.02.40 PM.png\" style=\"width: 641px;\"> <span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><em>Source: <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/6140493?hl=en\">Google</a></em></span> <p>You can add up to five cards to a single video, and there are six types:</p> \n   <ol> \n    <li>Channel cards that direct viewers to another channel.</li> \n    <li>Donation cards to encourage fundraising on behalf of U.S. nonprofit organizations.</li> \n    <li>Fan funding to ask your viewers to help support the creation of your video content.</li> \n    <li>Link cards, which direct viewers to an external site, approved crowdfunding platform, or an approved merchandise selling platform.</li> \n    <li>Poll cards, which pose a question to viewers and allow them to vote for a response.</li> \n    <li>Video or playlist cards, which link to other YouTube content of this kind.</li> \n   </ol> <p>For detailed steps on adding a card to your video, follow these <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/6140493?hl=en\">official steps</a> from Google, or check out the video below.</p> \n   <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"width: 100%; height: auto; position: relative; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; min-width: 256px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; margin: 0px auto;\"> \n    <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 59.38%; margin: 0;\"> \n     <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe hs-fullwidth-embed\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"http://www.youtube.com/embed/-Sex3r_CNWU\" width=\"640\" height=\"380\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </div> \n   </div> <h4>End Screens</h4> <p>End screens display similar information as cards, but as you may have guessed, they don't display until a video is over, and are a bit more visually detailed in nature. A good example is the overlay with a book image and a visual link to view more on the video below:</p> <img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202017-05-25%20at%206.09.28%20PM.png?width=669&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202017-05-25%20at%206.09.28%20PM.png\" alt=\"End screens displayed on a YouTube video\" width=\"669\" title=\"Screen Shot 2017-05-25 at 6.09.28 PM.png\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> <span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><em>Source: <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=uyB_GZNpCQE\">Jamie Oliver on YouTube</a></em></span> <p>There are a number of detailed instructions for adding end screens depending on what kind of platform you want to design them for, as well as different types of content allowed for them by YouTube. Google outlines the details for how to optimize for all of those considerations <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/6388789?co=GENIE.Platform%3DDesktop&amp;hl=en\">here</a>.</p> <p>It's important to note that YouTube is always testing end screens to try to optimize the viewer experience, so there are times when \"your end screen, as designated by you, may not appear.\" Take these factors into account as you decide between using either cards or end screens.</p> <p>These factors may seem a bit complicated and time-consuming, but remember: <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/marketing-statistics\">The time people spend watching YouTube on their TV has more than doubled year over year</a>. There's an audience to be discovered there, and when you optimize for YouTube, your chances of being discovered increase.</p> <p>Now, most of the SEO tips above rely on you identifying a keyword and promoting your video correctly. And not all of those tips can be carried out through YouTube alone. To get the most bang for your videography buck, consider some of the tools below to optimize your video for search.</p> <a></a> \n    <div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet\"> \n     <h2>YouTube SEO Tools</h2> \n     <ol> \n      <li>Ahrefs Keyword Explorer</li> \n      <li>Canva</li> \n      <li>HubSpot Content Strategy</li> \n      <li>VidIQ Vision</li> \n      <li>TubeBuddy</li> \n      <li>Cyfe</li> \n     </ol> \n    </div> <h3>1. <a href=\"https://ahrefs.com/keywords-explorer\">Ahrefs Keywords Explorer</a></h3> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/ahrefs-keyword-explorer-youtube.png?width=690&amp;name=ahrefs-keyword-explorer-youtube.png\" alt=\"ahrefs-keyword-explorer-youtube\" width=\"690\" style=\"width: 690px;\" /></p> <p>Ahrefs is a comprehensive SEO platform that allows you to monitor a website's ranking, estimate the organic traffic you'd get from each keyword, and research keywords for which you might want to create new content.</p> <p>One popular feature of Ahrefs is Keywords Explorer, which allows you to look up numerous details related to a keyword you're interested in. And as you can see in the screenshot above, you can filter your keyword results by search engine -- including YouTube.</p> <p>Ahrefs Keywords Explorer gives you a keyword's monthly search volume, how many clicks received by videos ranking for that keyword, related keywords, and more.</p> <h3>2. <a href=\"https://www.canva.com/create/youtube-thumbnails/\">Canva</a></h3> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/canva-youtube-thumbnail-designer.png?width=690&amp;name=canva-youtube-thumbnail-designer.png\" alt=\"canva-youtube-thumbnail-designer\" width=\"690\" style=\"width: 690px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" /></p> <p>You might know Canva as a design template for creating all kinds of cards, photos, logos, and more. It just so happens this popular product has a Thumbnail Creator just for YouTube videos.</p> <p>As stated in the tips above, thumbnail images are critical to promoting your content in YouTube search results and enticing users to click on your video. Using Canva's Thumbnail Creator, you can create the perfect preview image for your video in 1280 x 720 pixels -- the thumbnail dimensions YouTube requires.</p> <h3>3. <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/seo\">HubSpot Content Strategy</a></h3> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/hubspot-content-strategy-tool.jpg?width=690&amp;name=hubspot-content-strategy-tool.jpg\" alt=\"hubspot-content-strategy-tool\" width=\"690\" style=\"width: 690px;\">Our content strategy tool, developed here at HubSpot, allows you to find popular keywords for which to create content and then organize these keywords into groupings -- what we call \"topic clusters.\" By sorting your content into topic clusters, you can oversee which pieces of content are related to one another, which types of content you have planned, and what you've already created.</img></p> <p>While the keywords you discover in HubSpot reflect their popularity in a standard Google search, many of these topics will also produce videos on Google's search engine results pages. In those cases, you can create topic clusters that have both blog <em>and</em> YouTube content belonging to them.</p> <p>Clustering your content -- and linking from videos to blog posts, and vice-versa -- can give you more authority in the eyes of Google and YouTube, while giving you more ways to capture traffic from the people searching your topic.</p> <h3>4. <a href=\"https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/vidiq-vision-for-youtube/pachckjkecffpdphbpmfolblodfkgbhl?hl=en\">vidIQ Vision</a></h3> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/vidiq-vision-for-youtube.png?width=500&amp;name=vidiq-vision-for-youtube.png\" alt=\"vidiq-vision-for-youtube\" width=\"500\" style=\"width: 500px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\">This is a Chrome extension, available through Chrome's web store in the link above, that helps you analyze how and why certain YouTube videos perform so well. This includes the tags a video has been optimized for, its average watch time, and even how quickly that video might be gaining traffic.</img></p> <p>The vidIQ tool then provides an SEO \"score\" you can use to create content that performs (or outperforms) the results you already see on YouTube.</p> <h3>5. <a href=\"https://www.tubebuddy.com/tools#\">TubeBuddy</a></h3> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/tubebuddy-youtube-seo-tool.png?width=690&amp;name=tubebuddy-youtube-seo-tool.png\" alt=\"tubebuddy-youtube-seo-tool\" width=\"690\" style=\"width: 690px;\" /></p> <p>TubeBuddy is an all-in-one video platform that helps you manage the production, optimization, and promotion of your YouTube content. Its features include an automatic language translator (which helps you rank for non-English keywords), a keyword explorer, tag suggestions, a rank tracker for your published videos, and more.</p> <h3>6. <a href=\"https://www.cyfe.com/web-analytics-dashboard\">Cyfe</a></h3> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/cyfe-web-analytics-tool.png?width=690&amp;name=cyfe-web-analytics-tool.png\" alt=\"cyfe-web-analytics-tool\" width=\"690\" /></p> <p>Cyfe is a large software suite that offers, among other things, a web analytics platform. On this platform, you can track page performance across every website property you have content on -- including YouTube -- and where each page's traffic is coming from.</p> <p>In addition to traffic analytics, Cyfe can show you which keywords you're ranking for and which ones are most popular across various search engines. Sounds a lot like Google Analytics or Moz, right? That's because Cyfe has data from both of those tools, and more, built into it.</p> <p>No matter what SEO tip or tool you start with, a successful YouTube channel begins with good content. Make sure your viewers have something high-quality and relevant to watch when they find you. Want step-by-step help? 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"65 Photoshop Shortcuts to Help You Edit Photos Like a Pro [Bookmarkable]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/photoshop-keyboard-shortcuts-list","description":"<p>Have you ever accidentally wasted an entire day in Photoshop?</p> \n<p>I have. It's not like you start out aimlessly. You have a simple goal in mind, like cropping a photo, improving the resolution, or changing the size of the canvas. But then, you look at how many options there are -- and trying to figure out which buttons to press to execute a single task suddenly turns into an attempt to solve The Riddle of the Sphinx.</p> \n<p>Wouldn't it be nice if you could just press a button, and magically, do what you wanted to do? Well, we've got good news for you: It turns out there are a wealth of Photoshop shortcuts that pretty much work just that way.</p> \n<p>By pressing a few keys on your computer keyboard at the same time, you can select tools, manipulate images and layers, and even make adjustments to your project's canvas. But if we're being honest, if you're just starting out with the software, there might be far too many Photoshop shortcuts to remember them all. That's why we created this guide -- for you to bookmark and return to next time your design project leaves you stumped.</p> \n<p><strong>Note:</strong> All of these shortcuts can be accessed on PC and Mac, but sometimes, they're different on each operating system. We've included both types below, and in the cases where they might be different, Mac instructions appear in italicized parentheses. Also, in these formulas, the plus sign (+) is present only to represent the combination of key commands. On occasion, it might be part of the command itself, like when you press the plus sign to zoom into a part of an image, but otherwise, don't press the plus sign between commands.</p> \n<div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet\"> \n <h2>65 Photoshop Shortcuts to Save You Time</h2> \n <ol> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/photoshop-keyboard-shortcuts-list#setup\">Getting Set Up</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/photoshop-keyboard-shortcuts-list#tools\">Choosing the Right Tools</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/photoshop-keyboard-shortcuts-list#brushtool\">Using the Brush Tool</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/photoshop-keyboard-shortcuts-list#marqueetool\">Using the Marquee Tool (for Slicing/Selecting)</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/photoshop-keyboard-shortcuts-list#blendingoptions\">Using Different Blending Options</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/photoshop-keyboard-shortcuts-list#layersobjects\">Manipulating Layers &amp; Objects</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/photoshop-keyboard-shortcuts-list#savingwork\">Saving Your Work for Later</a></li> \n </ol> \n</div> \n<a></a> \n<h3>Getting Set Up</h3> \n<p>You'd think setting up your content in Photoshop would be second nature. But sometimes, the shortcuts to change the background size, or zoom into your project aren't what you think. Here are some of the most crucial fundamental shortcuts to know:</p> \n<p><strong>1) Control</strong> +<strong> Alt </strong>+<strong> i (<em>Command</em></strong><em> +<strong> Option </strong>+</em><strong><em> i </em>)</strong> = Change the image size.</p> \n<p><strong>2) Control </strong>+ <strong>Alt </strong>+ <strong>c (<em>Command</em></strong><em> +<strong> Option </strong>+</em><strong><em> c </em>)</strong> = Change canvas size.</p> \n<p><strong>3) Control </strong>+ <strong>+ (<em>Command </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> + </em>)</strong> = Zoom in.</p> \n<p><strong>4) Control </strong>+ <strong>- (<em>Command </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> - </em>)</strong> = Zoom out.</p> \n<p><strong>Control </strong>+<strong> ' (<em>Command </em></strong><em>+ </em><strong><em>' </em>)</strong> = Show or hide the <em>grid</em>, the automatically-generated horizontal and vertical lines that help align objects to the canvas.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>Choosing the Right Tools</h3> \n<p>These shortcuts will activate different groups of tools, like \"Lasso,\" \"Brush,\" or \"Spot Healing Brush.\" Within these tools, though, there are different functions. Under the \"Magic Wand\" tool group, for example, you have the option to execute a new selection or add and subtract from a current one.</p> \n<p>Each one of these tools has a keyboard shortcut, and we've outlined some of them below.</p> \n<p><strong>5) v </strong>= Pointer, a.k.a. Move Tool <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/pointer-tool.png?width=35&amp;height=28&amp;name=pointer-tool.png\" alt=\"pointer-tool.png\" title=\"pointer-tool.png\" width=\"35\" height=\"28\">&nbsp;</img></p> \n<p><strong>6)</strong> <strong>w</strong> = Magic Wand <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/magic-wand-tool.png?width=32&amp;height=31&amp;name=magic-wand-tool.png\" alt=\"magic-wand-tool.png\" title=\"magic-wand-tool.png\" width=\"32\" height=\"31\" /></p> \n<p><strong>7) m</strong> = Rectangular Marquee, a.k.a. the Select Tool <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/marquee-tool-1.png?width=29&amp;height=23&amp;name=marquee-tool-1.png\" alt=\"marquee-tool-1.png\" title=\"marquee-tool-1.png\" width=\"29\" height=\"23\" /></p> \n<p><strong>8) l</strong> = Lasso <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/lasso-tool.png?width=31&amp;height=25&amp;name=lasso-tool.png\" alt=\"lasso-tool.png\" /></p> \n<p><strong>13) t</strong> = Horizontal Type <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/text-tool.png?width=33&amp;height=30&amp;name=text-tool.png\" alt=\"text-tool.png\" 12.27.48 PM.png\" title=\"Screen Shot 2017-05-26 at 12.27.48 PM.png\" width=\"31\" style=\"width: 31px;\" /></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>Using the Brush Tool</h3> \n<p>With the brush settings, you can change the size, shape, and transparency of your brush strokes to achieve a number of different visual effects. To use these keyboard shortcuts, first select the Brush tool by pressing <strong style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\">b</strong>. <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/00-Blog-Related_Images/brush-tool.png?width=30&amp;height=23&amp;name=brush-tool.png\" alt=\"brush-tool.png\" title=\"brush-tool.png\" width=\"30\" height=\"23\" style=\"letter-spacing: 0px; background-color: transparent;\" /></p> \n<p><strong>29) , </strong>or<strong> . </strong>= Select previous or next brush style.</p> \n<p><strong>30) Shift </strong>+<strong> , </strong>or<strong> . </strong>= Select first or last brush style used.</p> \n<p><strong>31) Caps Lock or Shift </strong>+<strong> Caps Lock <em>(Caps Lock)</em></strong> = Display precise crosshair for brushes.</p> \n<p><strong>32) Shift </strong>+<strong> Alt </strong>+<strong> p<em> (Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> p)</em></strong> = Toggle airbrush option.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>Using the Marquee Tool (for Slicing/Selecting)</h3> \n<p>When used correctly, the marquee tool will let you select individual elements, entire graphics, and determine what is copied, cut, and pasted into your graphics.</p> \n<p>To use these keyboard shortcuts, first select the Marquee tool by pressing <strong>m</strong>. <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/marquee-tool-2.png?width=29&amp;height=23&amp;name=marquee-tool-2.png\" alt=\"marquee-tool-2.png\" title=\"marquee-tool-2.png\" width=\"29\" height=\"23\" /></p> \n<p><strong>33) Control <em>(Command)</em></strong> = Toggle between Slice tool and Slice Selection tool.</p> \n<p><strong>34) Shift </strong>+ <strong>drag</strong> = Draw square slice.</p> \n<p><strong>35) Alt </strong>+ <strong>drag <em>(Option </em></strong><em>+ </em><strong><em>drag)</em></strong> = Draw from center outward.</p> \n<p><strong>36) Shift </strong>+ <strong>alt</strong> + <strong>drag <em>(Shift </em></strong><em>+ <strong>option</strong> + <strong>drag) </strong></em>= Draw square slice from center outward.</p> \n<p><strong>37) Spacebar </strong>+ <strong>drag</strong> = Reposition the slice while creating the slice.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>Using Different Blending Options</h3> \n<p>Blending options include a number of features to enhance the look of your graphic. You can always choose a blending option by going to the top menu bar, under <strong>Layer</strong> &gt; <strong>Layer Style</strong> &gt; <strong>Blending Options. </strong>Or, you can double-click any layer to bring up the options for that particular layer.</p> \n<p>Once you open blending options, you can use keyboard shortcuts to select them without moving your mouse. To use the shortcuts, select the Move tool (\"<strong>v</strong>\"), and then select the layer you'd like to use the blending options on. Below are some of the most popular modes.</p> \n<p><strong>38) Shift </strong>+<strong> + </strong>or<strong> – </strong>= Cycle through blending modes.</p> \n<p><strong>39) Shift </strong>+<strong> Alt </strong>+<strong> n <em>(Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> n)</em></strong> = Normal mode</p> \n<p><strong>40) Shift </strong>+<strong> Alt </strong>+<strong> i <em>(Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> i)</em></strong> = Dissolve</p> \n<p><strong>41) Shift </strong>+<strong> Alt </strong>+<strong> k <em>(Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> k)</em></strong> = Darken</p> \n<p><strong>42) Shift </strong>+<strong> Alt </strong>+<strong> g <em>(Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> g)</em></strong> = Lighten</p> \n<p><strong>43) Shift </strong>+<strong> Alt </strong>+<strong> m <em>(Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> m)</em></strong> = Multiply</p> \n<p><strong>44) Shift </strong>+<strong> Alt </strong>+<strong> o <em>(Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> o)</em></strong> = Overlay</p> \n<p><strong>45) Shift + Alt + u <em>(Shift + Option + u)</em></strong> = Hue</p> \n<p><strong>46) Shift + Alt + t <em>(Shift + Option + t)</em></strong> = Saturation</p> \n<p><strong>47) Shift + Alt + y <em>(Shift + Option + y)</em></strong> = Luminosity</p> \n<p>For more niche blending shortcuts, check out <a href=\"https://helpx.adobe.com/photoshop/using/default-keyboard-shortcuts.html\">these tips</a> from Adobe.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>Manipulating Layers &amp; Objects</h3> \n<p>If you want to modify an object or get complex with multiple layers, here are some shortcuts you might like to know:</p> \n<p><strong>48) Control </strong>+<strong> a (<em>Command </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> a </em>)</strong> = Select all objects</p> \n<p><strong>49) Control </strong>+<strong> d (<em>Command </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> d </em>)</strong> = Deselect all objects</p> \n<p><strong><strong>50) Shift</strong> </strong>+<strong> <strong>Control</strong> </strong>+<strong> <strong>i</strong> (<em>Shift</em></strong><em> + <strong>Command</strong> + </em><strong><em>i </em>)</strong> = Select the inverse of the selected objects</p> \n<p><strong>51) Control </strong>+<strong> Alt </strong>+<strong> a <em>(Command </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> a)</em></strong> = Select all layers</p> \n<p><strong>52) Control </strong>+<strong> Shift </strong>+<strong> E <em>(Command </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> e)</em></strong> = Merge all layers</p> \n<p><strong>53) Alt </strong>+<strong> . <em>(Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> .)</em></strong> = Select top layer</p> \n<p><strong>54) Alt </strong>+<strong> , <em>(Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> ,)</em></strong> = Select bottom layer</p> \n<p><strong>Note</strong>: In shortcuts 55-57, the brackets (<strong>[ ]</strong>) are the keystrokes in the command, and \"OR\" refers to the actual word -- as in, press one bracket OR the other, not the letters \"o\" and \"r.\"</p> \n<p><strong>55) Alt </strong>+<strong> [ </strong>OR<strong> ] <em>(Option </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> [ </em></strong><em>OR</em><strong><em> ])</em></strong> = Select next layer down or up</p> \n<p><strong>56) Control </strong>+<strong> [ </strong>OR<strong> ] <em>(Command </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> [ </em></strong><em>OR</em><strong><em> ])</em> </strong>= Move target layer down or up</p> \n<p><strong>57) Control </strong>+<strong> Shift </strong>+<strong> [ </strong>OR<strong> ]<em> (Command </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> [ </em></strong><em>OR</em><strong><em> ])</em></strong> = Move layer to the bottom or top</p> \n<p><strong><strong>58) Shift</strong> </strong>+<strong> <strong>Control</strong></strong> + <strong><strong>n </strong><em>(Shift</em></strong><em> + <strong>Command</strong> + <strong>n)</strong></em> = Create a new layer</p> \n<p><strong><strong>59) Control </strong></strong>+<strong><strong> g <em>(Command </em></strong></strong><em>+ <strong>g<strong>)</strong> </strong></em>= Group selected layers</p> \n<p><strong>60) Control </strong>+<strong> Shift </strong>+<strong> g <em>(Command</em></strong><em> + <strong>Shift</strong> + <strong>g) </strong></em>= Ungroup selected layers</p> \n<p><strong>61) Control </strong>+<strong> e <em>(Command </em></strong><em>+ <strong>e)</strong></em> = Merge and flatten selected layers</p> \n<p><strong><strong><strong>62) Control</strong> </strong></strong>+<strong><strong> <strong>Shift</strong> </strong></strong>+<strong><strong> <strong>Alt</strong> </strong></strong>+<strong><strong> e<em><strong> (</strong></em></strong><em>Command</em></strong><em> + <strong>Shift</strong> + <strong>Option</strong> + <strong>e)</strong></em> = Combine all layers into a new layer <em>on top of </em>the other layers. Note: This step gets you one, combined layer, with all elements of that layer in separate layers below -- which is different than a traditional merge-and-flatten layers command.</p> \n<p><strong>63) Control </strong>+<strong> t <em>(Command </em></strong><em>+ <strong>t)</strong></em> = Transform your object, which includes resizing and rotating</p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>And Finally -- Save Your Work for Later</h2> \n<p>Congratulations -- you've finished working on your project, and now, you want to share it with the world. Save time saving your project by using these simple shortcuts:</p> \n<p><strong>64) Control</strong> + <strong>Shift</strong> + <strong>s <em>(Command </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> Shift </em></strong><em>+</em><strong><em> s)</em></strong> = Save your work as ...</p> \n<p><strong><strong>65) Control</strong> </strong>+<strong> <strong>Shift</strong> </strong>+<strong> <strong>Alt</strong> </strong>+<strong> <strong>s </strong><em>(Command</em></strong><em> + <strong>Shift</strong> + <strong>Option</strong> + <strong>s) </strong></em>= Save for web and devices</p>
