aderx/cdn74@2020_1/2020/11/14/17-30-24-941_d29cf1f7cdb369b7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605375018206},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"53 Focus Group Questions for Any Purpose","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/22025/5-focus-group-questions-to-feed-your-content-marketing.aspx","description":"<p>Whether your focus group is there to give feedback on a product or service or help you assess how your brand stands out in your competitive landscape, thought-provoking, open-ended questions are <em>essential</em> to a productive discussion.</p>  \n<p>However, it's easier said than done. What can you ask beyond <em>\"</em>What do you think of our product?\" that can provoke the most useful answers?</p> \n<p>Here, we've pulled together 53 questions you can ask in your next focus group to pull the most interesting and useful insights you can out of your participants.</p> \n<p><span style=\"color: #33475b; font-family: AvenirNext, 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 18px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: 400;\">Simply copy-and-paste the questions you like below into the notetaking template for a ready-to-go, printable document you can bring to the session.</span></p> \n<p style=\"font-size: 30px; text-align: center;\"><strong>Featured Resource: <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/market-research-kit?hubs-post_cta=body\">Market Research Focus Group Template</a></strong></p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202019-10-29%20at%203.00.45%20PM-3.png?width=566&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202019-10-29%20at%203.00.45%20PM-3.png\" width=\"566\" style=\"width: 566px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/market-research-kit?hubs-post_cta=body\">Download the Template</a></em></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: left;\">For a free template for notetaking during focus groups, a guide on conducting market research, and several other templates, download our <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/market-research-kit?hubs-post_cta=body\">Market Research Kit</a>.</p> \n<h3>Questions for Building Trust Among Focus Group Members</h3> \n<p>Before diving into deeper questions, it's best to warm up the group with a couple of open-ended questions that allow participants to get to know each other a little bit. Participants should be able to decide how much they want to share with the group -- don't force anyone to share something they may not feel comfortable sharing.</p> \n<p>By including a question that allows people to talk about something tangential to the topic of the focus group, your participants will begin to build empathy for each other. That empathy can grow into trust, which is key for eliciting honest insights out of your group.</p> \n<p>Here are a few questions you might ask to build trust:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Share an aspect of your work or life experience that's brought you here today.</li> \n <li>Why did you decide to join our focus group today?</li> \n <li>When and how did you first come across our brand/product/service?</li> \n</ul> \n<p></p> \n<h3>Questions to Encourage Follow-up and Continuation of Ideas</h3> \n<p>The most helpful insights that come out of focus groups are often the most specific points. Challenge your participants to reflect more on the points they've made if you hear something that you're curious about. For instance:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>That's a fascinating point that [name] just said -- what do you all think of that?</li> \n <li>Do you agree or disagree with [name]'s statement, and why?</li> \n <li>[Name], you've been a bit quiet recently. Did you have any thoughts on this topic that you wanted to share?</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Questions for Understanding Customer Perception of Your Product or Service</h3> \n<p>These questions will help you understand how people <em>truly</em> feel about your brand, product, or service. The focus here is on your company -- not the larger industry landscape or your competitors.</p> \n<p>Avoid stopping conversation here unless the group gets completely sidetracked. Open-ended questions can be daunting at first. Participants may not know where to start. However, hearing from the other participants will spark reflection on various aspects of your product or service. Be sure to allow each group member who has something to say to speak up before moving on to the next question.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>How would you describe our company to other people?</li> \n <li>How would you describe our product/service to other people?</li> \n <li>What words or feelings come to mind when you think about our company?</li> \n <li>How likely are you to recommend our product/service to a friend?</li> \n <li>How well do you feel we incorporate feedback from you, our customers, into our service/product?</li> \n <li>What ultimately pushed you to purchase this product/service?</li> \n <li>Where would you buy this product/service?</li> \n <li>What do you like about this product that you may not find in a similar one?</li> \n <li>When you think about our industry, which brands come to mind first?</li> \n <li>Which other brands in our industry did you consider when you were shopping around?</li> \n <li>Why didn't you go with one of our competitors?</li> \n <li>What other products/services come to mind when you look at this one?</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Questions to Learn What Your Leads and Customers Want to See From You</h3> \n<p>Listening to your customers' feedback and suggestions for improvement is crucial to retaining customers and turning them into promoters of your brand. It may be difficult to hear the answers to these questions, but turning customer pain points around will elevate your product or service to the next level.</p> \n<p>Avoid defending your product or service or setting any limitations on these questions. Instead, frame them in a way that allows anyone to voice anything at all that they're feeling. Recognize that it can be daunting for anyone (especially people with whom you've built relationships) to share negative feedback, so thank them for their candor.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>If you could wave a magic wand and change one thing about our product/service, what would it be?</li> \n <li>What would you most like to add to or improve about this product?</li> \n <li>What do you envision is the lifespan of this product/service before you upgrade or replace it?</li> \n <li>Is there anything we haven't touched on today that you'd like us to know?</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Questions for Understanding Your Buyer Personas</h3> \n<p>The following eight questions will help you understand what motivates your target <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buyer-persona-research\">buyer persona</a>, their habits, their responsibilities and decision-making power, and their preferences.</p> \n<p>These questions are written to spark discussion about topics other than your company, product or service, and the competitive landscape.</p> \n<p>Don't worry if the conversation seems to stray far from your brand, as the insights that people end up sharing will likely reveal what's significant to them in their life and work. However, it's important you keep the group focused on the specific question you've asked.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Describe your job title and your day-to-day responsibilities.</li> \n <li>What's one task on which you feel you spend way too much time?</li> \n <li>How do you define success in your role/your life?</li> \n <li>What is the biggest challenge you face in your role/when it comes to the problem to which this product is a solution?</li> \n <li>When you're browsing online, on which websites do you spend most of your time?</li> \n <li>What are the first three apps you open on your phone in the morning?</li> \n <li>How do you prefer to receive communications from our company? (Specify what type of communication here -- product updates, renewal notices, product/service coaching, meeting reminders, urgent alerts, etc.)</li> \n <li>Would you be the one using this product/service most in your household/job? If not, who would be?</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Questions for Getting a Better Sense of the Competitive Landscape</h3> \n<p>These questions are intended to spark discussion about the brands in your industry that are top-of-mind for consumers. These are helpful in removing any biases that you and your team might have as people who work in the industry and know various players very well.</p> \n<p>To encourage honesty, avoid agreeing with any disparaging comments that your participants make about your competitors. Instead, use the opportunity to ask follow-up questions about exactly what the participants don't like about a specific product or brand.</p> \n<p>If you're looking to do a complementary research-based analysis of your competitors, download our <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/market-research-kit?hubs-post_cta=body\">Market Research Kit</a> to gain access to a S.W.O.T. analysis template.</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/53%20Focus%20Group%20Questions%20for%20Any%20Purpose-1.png\" alt=\"\">\n</div> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/market-research-kit?hubs-post_cta=body\">Download the Template</a></em></p> \n<h3>Questions for Generating Content on Your Industry</h3> \n<p>You might be looking to <a href=\"https://academy.hubspot.com/courses/content-strategy\">develop a content strategy</a> for your brand, branch out into a new content medium, or simply generate new content ideas. Any successful content strategy prioritizes what's most engaging and interesting for your target buyer persona, so a focus group can be an effective way to be sure that you're producing material on the right topics and in the medium that your audience wants to consume.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>What is one recent trend you've noticed in our industry?</li> \n <li>What's one strategy or tactic you think is underrated in our industry?</li> \n <li>Where do you go to get a pulse on the things going on in our industry?</li> \n <li>Who are the people in our industry who you look to as experts?</li> \n <li>What format of content do you consume to keep up with our industry? Social media posts? Blogs/long-form posts? Podcasts? News outlets?</li> \n <li>Which specific sources do you go to for information on our industry?</li> \n <li>What gaps do you see in the content about our industry online? What are the topics on which you'd like to see more education?</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Questions for Understanding Product Demand for Something You Haven't Yet Put Out in the Market</h3> \n<p>These eleven questions are intended to help you understand the demand for a new product or service. These questions will uncover buying habits for a product like the one you're envisioning and whether there's true product-market fit.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>What is/was your first reaction to the product?</li> \n <li>How often do you/would you use this type of product?</li> \n <li>Would you be the one deciding to purchase this product/service? If not, who would be?</li> \n <li>When and where do you use our product?</li> \n <li>When you think about the product, do you think of it as something you absolutely need, something you could do without, or something that's somewhere in the middle?</li> \n <li>How much would you be willing to pay for a product like this?</li> \n <li>How would you ideally like to buy this product? Would you talk to a sales rep, or would you rather purchase it on your own?</li> \n <li>What do you think this product is missing?</li> \n <li>How would you describe someone who you think would use this product/service?</li> \n <li>If you ended up liking your experience with this product, could you see yourself repurchasing it? If so, how often?</li> \n <li>If you could either have this product/service or the equivalent dollar value for you/your business, which would you choose? Why? (Specify the dollar value of your product/service when asking this question.)</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Questions for Establishing (or Re-establishing) Your Name and Branding</h3> \n<p>The following questions are helpful for running word association brainstorms and generating potential names or parts of names for a new product or company.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>What words come to mind when you think of our product category? (Example: \"What words come to mind when you think of food delivery?\")</li> \n <li>What words come to mind when you think of [insert a word that symbolizes the main value prop of your product/service here - for example, 'efficiency,' 'speed,' 'health']?</li> \n <li>If you have candidate names already:</li> \n <ul> \n  <li>What is your initial reaction to this name?</li> \n  <li>What words come to mind when you hear this name?</li> \n  <li>How would you pronounce this? (Spell out the name on a piece of paper or whiteboard.)</li> \n </ul> \n</ul> \n<p>And there you have it! 53 questions you can ask in your next focus group. If you're unsure how to conduct a successful focus group, take a look at <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-run-a-focus-group\">How to Run a Focus Group for Your Business</a>.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fblog%2Ftabid%2F6307%2Fbid%2F22025%2F5-focus-group-questions-to-feed-your-content-marketing.aspx&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 12 Nov 2020 19:19:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"1f69ef6b15accbd9a897b43ba116f6ee","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"Lucy Alexander","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202019-10-29%20at%203.00.45%20PM-3.png?width=566&name=Screen%20Shot%202019-10-29%20at%203.00.45%20PM-3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn72@2020_3/2020/11/14/17-30-20-504_6f132d7d36ae4e10.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/53%20Focus%20Group%20Questions%20for%20Any%20Purpose-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn38@2020_5/2020/11/14/17-30-20-625_3135d311cf578ce5.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fblog%2Ftabid%2F6307%2Fbid%2F22025%2F5-focus-group-questions-to-feed-your-content-marketing.aspx&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn57@2020_3/2020/11/14/17-30-22-753_5aeec40a55b57645.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605375018183},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"What Is the 10/20/30 Rule of PowerPoint?","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/1056/steve-jobs-guy-kawasaki-powerpoint-best-practices.aspx","description":"<div class=\"hs-migrated-cms-post\"> \n <p>Despite how many PowerPoint presentations I’ve given in my life, I’ve always struggled with understanding the best practices for creating them. I know they need to look nice, but figuring out how to make them aesthetically pleasing and informative is tough.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>I’m sure my experience isn’t unique, as finding the correct balance between content, design, and timing can be difficult. Marketers know this more than anyone, as success in the role is often marked by being able to create engaging campaigns that tell a story and inspire audiences to take a specific action, like purchasing a product.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>However, PowerPoint presentations are different from advertisements. Understanding how to leverage your marketing knowledge when creating PowerPoints can be tricky. Still, there are various resources for marketers to use when creating presentations, one of which is the 10/20/30 rule.&nbsp;</p> \n <p></p> \n <p></p> \n <p>Coined by Guy Kawasaki, the rule is a tool for marketers to create excellent PowerPoint presentations. Each element of the formula helps marketers find a balance between design and conceptual explanations, so you can capture audience attention, emphasize your points, and enhance readability.&nbsp;</p> \n</div> \n<h2>Guy Kawasaki PowerPoint</h2> \n<p><a href=\"https://guykawasaki.com/\">Guy Kawasaki</a>, one of the early Apple employees, championed the concept of a ‘brand evangelist’ to describe his position. He spent most of his time working to generate a follower base for Macintosh, the family of Apple computers. Today he works as a brand evangelist for Canva, an online graphic design tool.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Given that he’s had significant experience giving presentations to captivate audiences, he’s figured out that the <a href=\"https://guykawasaki.com/the_102030_rule/\">10/20/30</a> is a successful formula to follow. Kawasaki’s book, <a href=\"https://guykawasaki.com/books/the-art-of-the-start/\">Art of The Start</a>, is where he first introduced the concept and described how it works.</p> \n<p>Let’s cover each part of the rule in more detail.&nbsp;</p> \n<h3>10 Slides</h3> \n<p>Kawasaki believes that it’s challenging for audiences to comprehend more than ten concepts during a presentation. Given this, marketers should aim to create PowerPoints with no more than ten slides, i.e., ten ideas you’ll explain. Using fewer slides and focusing on the critical elements helps your audience grasp the concepts you’re sharing with them.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>In practice, this means creating slides that are specific and straight to the point. For example, say you’re presenting on the success of your recent campaign. Your marketing strategy was likely extensive, and you took a series of different actions to obtain your end result. Instead of outlining every aspect of your campaign, you would use your slides to outline its main elements of your strategy. This could look like individual slides for summarizing the problem you hoped to solve, your goals, the steps you took to reach your goals, and post-campaign analytics data that summarizes your accomplishments.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>It’s important to note that there shouldn’t be overwhelming amounts of text on your slides. You want them to be concise. Your audience should get most of the information from the words you’re speaking; your slides should be more supplemental than explanatory.&nbsp;</p> \n<h3>20 Minutes</h3> \n<p>After you’ve spent time coming up with your ten key points, you’ll need to present them in 20 minutes. Knowing that you’ll only have 20 minutes also makes it easier to plan and structure your talk, as you’ll know how much time to dedicate to each slide, so you address all relevant points.</p> \n<p>Kawasaki acknowledges that presentation time slots can often be longer, but finishing at the 20-minute mark leaves time for valuable discussion and Q&amp;A. Saving time in your presentation also leaves space for technical difficulties.&nbsp;</p> \n<h3>30 Point Font</h3> \n<p>If you’ve been in the audience during a presentation, you probably know that slides with small font can be challenging to read and take your attention away from the speaker.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Kawasaki’s final rule is that no font within your presentation should be smaller than 30 point size. If you’ve already followed the previous rules, then you should be able to display your key points on your slides in a large enough font that users can read. Since your key points are short and focused, there won’t be a lot of text for your audience to read, and they’ll spend more time listening to you speak.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Given that the <a href=\"https://www.digitalauthority.me/resources/ada-compliant-font-size/#:~:text=What's%20the%20right%20size%20font,font%20for%20the%20body%20text.\">average recommended font size</a> for accessibility is 16, using a 30-point font ensures that all members of your audience can read and interact with your slides.&nbsp;</p> \n<h2>Make Your Presentations More Engaging</h2> \n<p>The 10/20/30 rule of PowerPoint is meant to help marketers create powerful presentations.&nbsp;</p> \n<p class=\"hs-migrated-cms-post\">Each element of the rule works in tandem with the other: limiting yourself to 10 slides requires you to select the most salient points to present to your audience. A 20-minute timeline helps you ensure that you’re contextualizing those slides as you speak, without delving into unnecessary information. Using a 30-point font can act as a final check for your presentation, as it emphasizes the importance of only displaying key points on your slides, rather than huge blocks of text. Font size then circles back around to the ten slides, as you’ll craft sentences from your key points that will fit on your slides in 30-point font.&nbsp;</p> \n<p class=\"hs-migrated-cms-post\">Being mindful of slide count, text size, and presentation length ensures that your audiences are captivated by your words as you explain the value behind your work.&nbsp;</p> \n<p class=\"hs-migrated-cms-post\"></p> \n<p class=\"hs-migrated-cms-post\">  </p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fblog%2Ftabid%2F6307%2Fbid%2F1056%2Fsteve-jobs-guy-kawasaki-powerpoint-best-practices.aspx&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 12 Nov 2020 12:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"775ac25bb5e7d660f8d604fc6f7c94cd","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"bhalligan@hubspot.com (Brian Halligan)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fblog%2Ftabid%2F6307%2Fbid%2F1056%2Fsteve-jobs-guy-kawasaki-powerpoint-best-practices.aspx&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn17@2020_2/2020/11/14/17-30-24-428_93ac085e0bd011aa.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605375018184},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"How to Tell a Compelling Brand Story [Guide + Examples]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/brand-story","description":"<p>Last year, a buzzword ripped through the content marketing space that most marketers were surprisingly thrilled about and eager to implement. Shockingly, it didn’t start with “virtual” or end with “intelligence”. Instead, it was what attracted most marketers to the industry in the first place -- \"storytelling\".</p>  \n<p>Content marketing’s steady adoption of storytelling is an exciting new opportunity for content creators.&nbsp;The human brain is <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/the-strange-thing-that-happens-in-you-brain-when-you-hear-a-good-story-and-how-to-use-it-to-your-advantage\">wired to respond to well-crafted narrative</a> -- neuroscience proves that storytelling is the best way to capture people’s attention, bake information into their memories, and forge close, personal bonds. Your audience is programmed to crave and seek out great stories -- that’ll never change.</p> \n<p>However,&nbsp;since we’ve spent the majority of our careers optimizing content for algorithms, it can be challenging to flex a creative muscle that’s slowly withered away from inactivity and, in turn, move people emotionally and sear your brand into their memories.</p> \n<p>So, to help you strengthen that creative muscle and write compelling stories again, we’ve created a guide about the fundamentals of brand story structure and provided examples of three small-to-medium sized businesses who have leveraged their brand story to resonate with huge audiences, despite their comparatively small size.</p> \n<p></p> \n<div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet\"> \n <h2>What is a brand story?</h2> \n <p>A brand story recounts the series of events that sparked your company’s inception and expresses how that narrative still drives your mission today. Just like your favorite books and movies’ characters, if you can craft a compelling brand story, your audience will remember who you are, develop empathy for you, and, ultimately, care about you.</p> \n</div> \n<p>When HubSpot first started, we noticed traditional, interruptive marketing didn’t appeal to consumers anymore. Due to the digital age, people were in complete control of the information they consumed -- and they were sick and tired of receiving direct mail, email blasts, and cold calls. People wanted to be helped, so we started creating educational content that aided people in solving their marketing problems.</p> \n<p>Today, we’ve built a passionate community of inbound marketers, expanded our inbound marketing approach to the sales and customer service industries, and strengthened the inbound movement more than ever before.</p> \n<p>This our brand story -- a simple, digestible narrative that&nbsp;explains&nbsp;why HubSpot began, and how this reason still serves as our purpose today.</p> \n<h2>How to Write a Brand Story</h2> \n<h3>1. Highlight your story’s conflict.</h3> \n<p>Check out the following story. Does it resonate with you?</p> \n<p>A girl wearing a red-hooded cloak is strolling through the woods to give her sick grandma some much-needed food and TLC. She passes by a wolf on the way. They exchange a slightly awkward soft smile-nod combination that random colleagues usually greet each other with as they pass in the hallway. She makes it to her grandma’s house without a scratch. They eat lunch and play a game of Clue together. Grandma wins by deducing that Colonel Mustard killed Mr. Boddy in the Billiard Room with the candlestick -- what a shocker! The End.</p> \n<p>So ... what’d you think? Did this story keep you on the edge of your seat? Or does it feel … off? For some reason, it doesn’t work, right? That’s because there’s no conflict. Despite the intense game of Clue at the end, there’s nothing at stake. There’s no tension. The wolf didn’t try to eat the girl. He didn’t even go to Grandma’s house. He barely acknowledged Little Red Riding Hood.</p> \n<p>At their core, stories are about overcoming adversity. So if there’s no conflict presented, there’s no drama or emotional journey that people can relate to. And if your story has no drama or emotional journey, it won’t hold anyone’s attention -- let alone resonate with and inspire them.</p> \n<p>Unfortunately, in the business world, brands are horrified to reveal any adversity or conflict they’ve faced. They believe that spinning a rosy, blemish-free story about how their company only experiences hockey stick growth will convince people that they’re the industry’s best-in-class solution. Any adversity or conflict during their company’s history will expose their imperfections, deterring potential customers from buying their product.</p> \n<p>But, in reality, this is a huge misconception. Nothing’s perfect. Everything, including companies (<em>especially</em> companies), has flaws. Plus, people don’t relate to perfection. They relate to the emotional journey of experiencing adversity, struggling through it, and, ultimately, overcoming it. Because, in a nutshell, that’s the story of life.</p> \n<p>Conflict is key to telling compelling stories. So be transparent about the adversity your company has faced, and own it. The more honest you are about your shortcomings, the more people will respect you and relate to your brand.</p> \n<h3>2. Don’t forget about your story’s status quo and resolution.</h3> Conflict isn’t the only thing you should focus on when crafting your brand story. A compelling story has two other fundamental elements -- the status quo and resolution. \n<p>The status quo is the way things are or the initial nature of your situation. The conflict disrupts this situation and puts something at stake, forcing the protagonist (your brand) to actively find a solution to this problem. The resolution describes how the protagonist solves the problem, giving your audience an emotional payoff.</p> \n<p>In sum, your brand’s story structure should look like this -- status quo, conflict, and resolution. It’s as simple as that.</p> \n<p>If you need an example to crystalize brand story structure in your mind, let’s go over the actual Little Red Riding Hood story, as well as some brands who are nailing their brand stories right now.</p> \n<h4>Little Red Riding Hood</h4> \n<p><strong>Status Quo:</strong> Little Red Riding Hood walks through the woods, on her way to deliver food to her sick grandma.</p> \n<p><strong>Conflict:</strong> A Big Bad Wolf approaches her, and asks where she’s going. She naively tells him where her grandmother’s house is, so he suggests she picks some flowers as a present for her. While she’s distracted, he breaks into Little Red Riding Hood’s grandmother's house, eats her, and puts on her clothes to impersonate her.</p> \n<p>When Little Red Riding Hood gets to her grandmother’s house, she notices some subtle changes in her grandmother appearance but ultimately ignores them and hops into bed with her. The wolf swallows her whole. He falls asleep from a massive food coma.</p> \n<p><strong>Resolution:</strong> A hunter hears Little Red Riding Hood’s screams, bursts through grandma’s door, and cuts open the wolf’s stomach, setting Little Red Riding Hood and her grandmother free. They then fill the wolf’s body with heavy stones, and when he wakes up and tries to run away, he topples over and dies.</p> \n<p>Now -- wouldn’t you say that was a little more compelling and entertaining than finding out Colonel Mustard can wield a candlestick as a murder weapon? I would, too.</p> \n<p>The thing is, some small brands are leveraging this same exact story structure to generate massive amounts of brand awareness and affinity. Read on to find out exactly how they do it.</p> \n<div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet\"> \n <h2>Brand Story Examples</h2> \n <ol> \n  <li>Unthinkable Media</li> \n  <li>Grado Labs</li> \n  <li>Drift</li> \n </ol> \n</div> \n<h3>1.&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.unthinkablemedia.com/\">Unthinkable Media</a></h3> \n<p>Unthinkable Media is a creative agency that produces original, narrative-driven podcasts for B2B brands. Their mission is to create refreshing, entertaining shows for clients that can actually retain people’s attention, not just acquire it.</p> \n<p>Here’s a rundown of their brand story, which is also fleshed out in one of the founder’s <a href=\"http://jayacunzo.com/blog/one-simple-story-better-brand-storytelling\">blog posts</a>:</p> \n<p><strong>Status Quo:</strong> As makers and marketers, we want our audience’s attention, and so for years, we focused our efforts on acquiring it.</p> \n<p><strong>Conflict:</strong> But today, thanks to multiple screens, ubiquitous and instantly accessible content, and endless choice in nearly every competitive niche, the buyer now has total control. They only choose experiences they genuinely enjoy. It is no longer enough for us to simply acquire our audience's attention.</p> \n<p><strong>Resolution:</strong> We need to hold it. That is our new mandate as makers and marketers. We need to shift our focus from impressions and traffic to subscribers and community. Everything we are trying to achieve becomes possible and gets easier when our audience spends minutes or even hours with us, not seconds. Don't just acquire attention. Hold it.</p> \n<h3>2.&nbsp;<a href=\"https://gradolabs.com/\">Grado Labs</a></h3> \n<p>Grado Labs is a third-generation, family-owned headphone and cartridge company. They don’t believe in advertising, have operated in the same building for over a century, and even make their headphones by hand. So why do they choose to operate like this when huge brands like Beats by Dre, Sony, and Bose have celebrity endorsers and mass-produce their headphones? Check out our interpretation of their brand story to find out.</p> \n<p><strong>Status Quo:</strong> Music is an essential part of the human experience. Without it, life just isn’t as colorful and exciting. And we believe quality headphones amplify the pleasant, emotional experience of listening to music.</p> \n<p><strong>Conflict:</strong> In a market where every headphone brand has an enormous advertising budget, state-of-the-art facilities, and high-tech machines that can churn out as much product as they want, all of which we don’t have, why do we choose to not conform?</p> \n<p><strong>Resolution:</strong> Sound comes first. We’re craft-driven creators, meaning we prioritize producing the best product over generating the most hype. And by creating a better pair of headphones at the expense of publicity and growth, we can serve our customers better and foster a fervent passion for our product.</p> \n<h3>3.&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.drift.com/\">Drift</a></h3> \n<p>Drift is a conversational marketing platform that helps businesses connect with prospects through genuine, empathetic conversations and interactions. In 2016, <a href=\"https://www.drift.com/blog/forms-vs-conversations-data/\">they shocked the content marketing world</a> by scrapping arguably the most reliable lead generator from their website -- forms.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.drift.com/blog/unlock-unprecedented-growth/\">Even though they were initially anxious</a> about getting rid of a lead generation machine, they knew ungating every piece of content on their website would allow them to align with their mission, put their customers first, and offer as much value as possible, which would produce better long-term results. Here’s our interpretation of their brand story.</p> \n<p><strong>Status Quo:</strong> The crux of content marketing is treating people like humans. So, we’ve done what most other companies have done: created content that aims to help and educate our customers. And in exchange for adding value to their lives, customers are likely to return the favor with their attention, trust, and action.</p> \n<p><strong>Conflict:</strong> But as much as we preach about putting the customer first, we don’t practice it. Instead of offering the most value we possibly can, we make people give us their contact information in exchange for the very thing we promise is free. Then, with their contact information, we email and call them until they either unsubscribe or eventually buy. No one actually enjoys filling out forms, becoming a lead, and getting nurtured. Our ulterior motive is crystal clear. So are we actually being customer-centric?</p> \n<p><strong>Resolution:</strong> Let’s get rid of all our forms. If we really want to practice what we preach -- putting our customers first and providing a more human and empathetic marketing experience -- we should offer all of our content for free, with no strings attached.</p> \n<h3>Tell your brand’s real story, not it’s highlight reel.</h3> \n<p>Whether you’re publishing your brand story on your website or using it to inform your overall mission, make sure it’s fact, not fiction. Spitting out a highlight reel, like almost every other brand does, won’t actually resonate with people. Instead, it's crucial you tell the honest truth about the adversity your company has faced, and how you’re working to overcome it. Because what people relate to and get inspired by isn’t endless success -- it’s the rocky journey of pursuing a goal, getting knocked down, and, ultimately, finding a path toward success.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fbrand-story&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 04 Nov 2020 18:27:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"6e5d4019bcd2cd9ad34fd9a4d3769f50","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"cchi@hubspot.com (Clifford Chi)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fbrand-story&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn6@2020_6/2020/11/14/17-30-24-186_875c253fa2507219.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605375018204},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"The Ultimate Guide to B2B Marketing in 2020","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/b2b-marketing","description":"<p>Effective marketing is difficult to get right. Between creative demands, budget limits, and channel decisions, marketers have a lot to juggle when developing their marketing strategy.</p> \n<p>The biggest determinant of effective marketing, however, is your <em>audience</em>.</p> \n<p>If you’re not properly targeting your buyer persona, your promotions and advertisements will likely fall on deaf ears. You might as well not be marketing at all.</p> \n<p>Where target audiences vary the most, though, is between <strong>individual consumers and businesses</strong>. Some companies serve individual shoppers, while others cater to companies and organizations.</p> \n<p>Marketing to businesses is <em>very different</em> than marketing to individual consumers. That’s why an entirely different marketing method — B2B marketing — exists, and that’s why we built this guide. By the end of this article, you’ll have a better understanding of B2B marketing, the most effective B2B marketing strategies, and how you can tap into and convert your business audience.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p></p> \n<p><a></a></p> \n<p>HubSpot is an example of a company that engages in B2B marketing. HubSpot’s customers are other businesses, not individual consumers. Therefore, all of our marketing efforts can be classified as B2B.</p> \n<h2><a></a>B2B vs B2C Marketing</h2> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/agency/differences-b2c-b2b-marketing\">B2B and B2C (business-to-consumer) marketing</a> are very different. B2B and B2C marketing differ in their respective strategies and applications, as well as <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/b2b-b2c-content-marketing\">in their audiences and how they communicate to them</a>.</p> \n<p><strong>B2B marketing</strong> targets the needs, interests, and challenges of individuals who are making purchases on behalf of, or for, their organization (rather than for themselves), thus making the <em>organization</em> the customer. Here are a few examples of B2B companies:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>A coworking space that leases office spaces to remote teams and freelancers (like <a href=\"https://www.wework.com/\">WeWork</a>)</li> \n <li>An on-demand order fulfillment, warehousing, and screen printing service (like <a href=\"https://www.printful.com/\">Printful</a>)</li> \n <li>A marketing software company that sells social media management tools, lead generation software, and other marketing tools to businesses and organizations (like <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing\">HubSpot</a>!)</li> \n</ul> \n<p><strong>B2C marketing</strong> targets the needs, interests, and challenges of individual consumers who are making purchases on behalf of, or for, themselves, thus making the <em>individual</em> the customer. Here are a few examples of B2C companies:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>An e-commerce company that sells office supplies to remote or self-employed individuals (like <a href=\"https://www.poppin.com/\">Poppin</a>)</li> \n <li>A store that sells t-shirts and other clothing and accessories (like <a href=\"https://www.target.com/\">Target</a>)</li> \n <li>A music platform that sells streaming subscriptions (like <a href=\"https://www.spotify.com/\">Spotify</a>)</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Take a look at this chart comparing B2B and B2C customers.</p> \n<table style=\"width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">&nbsp;</td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\"><strong>for b2b marketing</strong></td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\"><strong>for b2c marketing</strong></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\"><strong>Goal</strong></td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers are focused on ROI, efficiency, and expertise.</td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers are seeking deals and entertainment (which means marketing needs to be more <em>fun</em>).</td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\"><strong>Purchase Motivation</strong></td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers are driven by logic and financial incentive.</td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers are driven by emotion.</td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\"><strong>Drivers</strong></td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers want to be educated (which is where <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/b2b-marketing#b2b-content-marketing\">B2B content marketing</a> comes in).</td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers appreciate education but don’t always need it to make a purchase decision.</td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\"><strong>Purchase Process</strong></td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers like (if not prefer) to work with account managers and salespeople.</td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers like to make purchases directly.</td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\"><strong>People Involved in Purchase</strong></td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers often have to confer with decision makers and other members of their chain of command before making a purchase decision.</td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers rarely need to confer with others before making a purchase decision.</td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\"><strong>Purchase Purpose</strong></td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers make purchases for long-term solutions, resulting in a longer sales cycle, longer contracts, and longer relationships with companies.</td> \n   <td style=\"width: 33.3333%;\">Customers aren’t necessarily looking for long-term solutions or long-term relationships.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>As much as they differ, though, B2B and B2C also intersect in many ways. While Poppin sells office supplies to remote or self-employed individuals, they also design corporate office spaces and branded supplies. On the flip side, Printful not only offers order fulfillment and warehousing to businesses; they also fill e-commerce printing orders for individuals.</p> \n<p>As distinct as the B2B and B2C marketing audiences can be, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/agency/b2c-campaigns-b2b-marketers-learn\">B2B marketers can always learn from B2C campaigns</a>, too.</p> \n<h2><a></a>B2B Marketing Strategies</h2> \n<p>As I said above, marketing depends on its audience. While B2B and B2C marketing vary, not every piece of B2B marketing material is alike, either.</p> \n<p>In this section, we’ll talk about various <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/b2b-customer-marketing\">B2B marketing strategies</a> you can implement to reach your <em>specific</em> business audience. Before we dive in, though, make sure you understand the B2B <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/what-is-the-buyers-journey\">buyer’s journey</a>. Take note of how each of these stages may affect your marketing strategies and how you implement them.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/b2b-marketing-buyers-journey-hubspot.png?width=600&amp;name=b2b-marketing-buyers-journey-hubspot.png\" alt=\"b2b-marketing-buyers-journey-hubspot\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\" /></p> \n<h3>B2B Email Marketing</h3> \n<p>Email marketing is a tried and true method of reaching both individual consumers and business customers. Did you know that <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/email-marketing-stats\">93% of B2B marketers</a> use email? Are you one of them? You should be. Emails lead to engagement which turns subscribers into leads … and then <em>customers</em>.</p> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/free-guide-to-optimizing-email-marketing-for-conversions?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase\">Download our guide to optimizing email marketing for conversions and learn how to grow your email list, ensure deliverability, and increase </a><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/free-guide-to-optimizing-email-marketing-for-conversions\">engagement</a><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/free-guide-to-optimizing-email-marketing-for-conversions\">.</a></em></p> \n<p>Unlike B2C customers who respond best to emotions and entertainment, B2B customers look for logic and positive ROI. Essentially, they’re asking themselves, <em>How can your business help my business grow?</em> Because of this, your email marketing must consistently resonate with your business customers and focus on things that matter to them — like time, money, and resources.</p> \n<p>Email marketing is also a powerful vehicle for sharing your brand’s content. <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/email-marketing-stats\">83% of B2B companies</a> use email newsletters as part of their content marketing program, and 40% of B2B marketers say these newsletters are <em>most</em> critical to their content marketing success.</p> \n<p>With the constant barrage of emails flooding our inboxes today, it’s more important than ever to create and send out effective marketing emails.</p> \n<h4>B2B Email Marketing Best Practices</h4> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Write enticing subject lines.</strong> Think about your email subject lines as a Netflix trailer — if you can’t hook your audience with a two-minute clip (or, in this case, a few dozen characters), don’t expect them to open and watch (or read) the whole thing. We recommend spending almost as much time on your email subject lines as you do on the emails themselves.</li> \n <li><strong>Stick to one call-to-action (CTA) per email.</strong> If you think the number of emails you receive is a lot, take a look at the <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/marketing-statistics\">CTAs in those emails</a> … some are packed with two, three, and sometimes up to 10 different CTAs. Don’t make this mistake, which can leave your recipients’ heads spinning, asking “What should I click on first?” and ultimately clicking on <em>nothing</em>. With one CTA per email, you allow your audience to focus on your email content and ultimately one action … a welcome reprieve from today’s frequent decision-making and analysis paralysis.</li> \n <li><strong>Segment your email to reach the most relevant audience. </strong>Not every email you send will be appropriate for everyone on your list. Your subscribers may be at different stages of the buyer’s journey or be seeking different solutions. That’s where <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/32848/Why-List-Segmentation-Matters-in-Email-Marketing.aspx\">email list segmentation</a> comes into play. Not only does this help you relate to your audience better, but it gives your emails that personal feel that says “Hey, I’m listening and I know what you’d like to see.” Consumers prefer email quality over quantity anytime.</li> \n <li><strong>Make sure your email designs are responsive.</strong> Over 80% of email users access their inbox on their phones, and emails that don’t show up correctly on mobile devices are often <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/marketing-statistics\">deleted in three seconds</a>. Ouch. Don’t let your email be one of those.</li> \n <li><strong>Don’t be afraid of the cold email.</strong> As uncomfortable as it is, the right email can convert new customers — like this <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/the-cold-email-template-that-won-16-new-b2b-customers\">cold sales email that won 16 new B2B customers</a>.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>👉🏼<strong>HubSpot Tip</strong>: You can’t send marketing emails without any recipients — these people make up your lists. There are plenty of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/32028/25-Clever-Ways-to-Grow-Your-Email-Marketing-List.aspx\">easy ways to grow your email list</a>. Begin with opt-in forms on your website homepage, About page, and blog. Check out <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/forms\">HubSpot’s Free Form Builder tool</a> to get started.</p> \n<h3>B2B Digital Marketing</h3> \n<p>Every business, whether B2B or B2C should have a digital presence — which is comprised of paid ads, search engine optimization, a website, and any other place your B2B company is active online. Let’s walk through a handful of tactics that can strengthen your B2B digital marketing strategy.</p> \n<h5>Define your target audience</h5> \n<p>A strong B2B digital marketing strategy starts with defining your target audience, or <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buyer-persona-research\">buyer persona</a>. This demographic and psychographic information will inform almost every other marketing activity thereafter, ensuring your content and digital material is absorbed by the right eyes and ears (and that no resources go to waste on your end).</p> \n<h5>Create your website</h5> \n<p>Secondly, digital marketing can’t quite function without an informative, engaging website. Over <a href=\"https://www.adweek.com/digital/81-shoppers-conduct-online-research-making-purchase-infographic/\">80% of buyers</a> visit a website before making a purchase. Moreover, since the typical B2B sales cycle often involves many key players (such as <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/identify-sales-prospects-influencers-decision-makers-ht\">gatekeepers, decision makers</a>, and other folks who have to buy into a purchase), websites are easy, straightforward ways for influencers to share information about your product or service.</p> \n<h5>Optimize your digital presence</h5> \n<p>Your website needs to be more than informative and engaging, though … it needs to be discoverable. You can do this with <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33655/a-step-by-step-guide-to-flawless-on-page-seo-free-template.aspx\">on-page SEO</a> and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/technical-seo\">technical SEO</a> tactics. These include everything from image alt-text and meta descriptions (what your visitors can see) to structured data and site speed (what your visitors can’t see). <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/6487/The-ABCs-of-Off-Page-SEO-Tactics.aspx\">Off-page SEO</a> is also at play here, which refers to external linking strategies and social sharing — SEO tactics that take place <em>off</em> your website.</p> \n<h5>Run PPC campaigns</h5> \n<p>Finally, round out your digital presence with <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/ppc\">pay-per-click (PPC) advertising</a>, which allows you to get your content and brand in front of new audiences via search engines and other advertising platforms. I recommend maximizing your PPC investment by advertising more than your specific products or services — such as your brand personality, blog or social media content, or company tagline.</p> \n<p>The best way to see an ROI from your paid ads is by 1) incorporating your buyer persona data and 2) boosting content that they can relate to. For example, it’s highly unlikely a brand new consumer who’s never heard of you is searching for your exact product. They may be searching for a location-based solution or product feature. To reach the greatest number of potential customers, pay to target relevant categories within your brand vs. promoting your product or services.</p> \n<h3><a></a>B2B Content Marketing</h3> \n<p>We’ve talked about how B2B customers are focused on expertise, driven by logic, and desire to be educated. What better marketing tool to satisfy these priorities than B2B content marketing?</p> \n<p>Whereas a traditional PR marketing strategy interrupts a consumer’s day-to-day with promotional material, a content marketing strategy adds valuable information and informs the consumer — which is precisely what B2B customers are looking for. Not to mention that content marketing supports SEO efforts, which involves <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/google-search-statistics\">anticipating what your audience is searching for</a>, helping them discover your website and content … and potentially converting them to customers.</p> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/b2b-vs-b2c-content-lessons?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase\">Download our free guide and learn what topics convert at the highest rate with insight from 175,000 B2B &amp; B2C blog posts.</a><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/b2b-vs-b2c-content-lessons\"></a></em></p> \n<p>In fact, <a href=\"https://b2bprblog.marxcommunications.com/b2bpr/top-b2b-pr-mistakes-to-avoid?utm_content=10778068&amp;utm_medium=social&amp;utm_source=Webbiquity.com\">80% of business decision makers</a> prefer to get information from an article than an ad. Knowing this, I’d say you should be putting the same (if not more) resources into your content marketing than your traditional advertising strategy.</p> \n<p>Because the B2B buyer’s journey is slightly different than the B2C buyer’s journey (which has shorter sales cycles and fewer decision makers involved), the content you create for your B2B content marketing strategy may vary more than the content you’ve seen as a consumer yourself, as illustrated in the below graphic.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/b2b-marketing-content-for-the-buyers-journey-graphic.png?width=600&amp;name=b2b-marketing-content-for-the-buyers-journey-graphic.png\" alt=\"b2b-marketing-content-for-the-buyers-journey-graphic\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\" /></p> \n<p>Before you start creating content, though, I recommend creating a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/47/engineering-blog-readership-7-ways-to-drive-prospects-to-your-small-business.aspx\">business blog</a>. (Don’t worry, <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/blog-readers\">growing your blog readership</a> is easier than you think.) Your blog will house all the content you create and serve as a home-base for readers to visit and subscribe to.</p> \n<h3>B2B Social Media Marketing</h3> \n<p>Did you know that <a href=\"https://www.idg.com/blog/5-statistics-will-change-view-b2b-buyers-journey/\">75% of B2B buyers and 84% of C-Suite executives</a> use social media when making a purchase? That’s right — social media marketing isn’t just for brands targeting individual consumers.</p> \n<p>Many B2B companies struggle with social media marketing, though. It can be harder to use social media to connect with business customers, especially because (as we mentioned above) there’s typically a lengthier sales cycle and longer chain of command.</p> \n<p>Honestly, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/32765/how-b2b-marketers-can-succeed-on-the-6-big-social-networks.aspx\">B2B social media marketing</a> might not be where you convert the greatest number of leads, and that’s OK. It likely comes into play near the beginning of your customers’ buyer’s journeys.</p> \n<p>Social media is a powerful tool for building brand awareness, giving your company an online personality, and humanizing your business — all very powerful factors when it comes to marketing and connecting with potential customers. Like email marketing, social media is also a highly effective channel for sharing your content and enhancing your brand expertise, the latter of which we know B2B customers appreciate.</p> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/social-inbox?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase\">Overwhelmed by social media? Spend more time connecting with your followers with our time-saving suite of social tools.</a></em></p> \n<p>While your social media accounts might not convert as frequently as your content or email marketing, they’re just as important. In this case, followers are just as valuable — you never know when they might convert to leads or customers.</p> \n<p>👉🏼 <strong>HubSpot Tip</strong>: Why? Content shared by employee advocates <a href=\"https://www.socialmediatoday.com/content/employee-advocate-mobilize-your-team-share-your-brand-content\">receives over eight times more engagement</a> than content shared by brands. So, involve your employees in your B2B social media marketing strategy. Encourage them to create their own social media channels and share about life at your company. Create a culture account (<a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/hubspotlife/\">like our @HubSpotLife Instagram</a>) to show what’s going on at work, not just what you’re selling. You never know — this might attract strong talent, too.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/b2b-marketing-social-media-employee-engagement-hubspot-life-instagram.png?width=600&amp;name=b2b-marketing-social-media-employee-engagement-hubspot-life-instagram.png\" alt=\"b2b-marketing-social-media-employee-engagement-hubspot-life-instagram\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\" /></p> \n<h2><a></a>B2B Marketing Examples</h2> \n<p>A B2B marketing approach that works for one business may not work for another, but that’s not to say we can’t learn something from the pros. Here are four <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/b2b-content-marketing-examples\">B2B marketing examples</a> of businesses who did it right.</p> \n<h3>Email Marketing: Mattermark, Raise the Bar Newsletter</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://mattermark.com/category/raise-the-bar/\">Raise the Bar</a> is a daily digest newsletter from Mattermark that features insights from leaders in sales, marketing, and growth engineering. It’s hand-picked by Mattermark executives and easy to scan, which is valuable in a world of elaborate, complicated newsletters and daily digests.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/b2b-marketing-email-marketing-mattermark-raise-the-bar.png?width=600&amp;name=b2b-marketing-email-marketing-mattermark-raise-the-bar.png\" alt=\"b2b-marketing-email-marketing-mattermark-raise-the-bar\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\" /></p> \n<p>This is a good example of B2B email marketing because Mattermark takes the time to educate their subscribers without blatantly selling to them. This action builds trust with their audience while also equipping them with everything they need to know to make a purchase and become a paying customer.</p> \n<h3>Digital Marketing: Maersk, Website Homepage</h3> \n<p>It’s nearly impossible to know the intent of everyone who lands on your website, but <a href=\"https://www.maersk.com/\">Maersk’s homepage design</a> makes it easy for visitors to find their way around.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/b2b-marketing-digital-marketing-maersk-homepage.png?width=600&amp;name=b2b-marketing-digital-marketing-maersk-homepage.png\" alt=\"b2b-marketing-digital-marketing-maersk-homepage\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\"><em><span style=\"font-size: 13px;\"><a href=\"https://www.maersk.com/\">Source</a></span></em></img></p> \n<p>By offering three main options (“Become a Customer,” “Access Your Account,” and “Start a Career”), Maersk clearly segments their audience and allows visitors to easily navigate to the site content that corresponds with their intent.</p> \n<p>This small design tweak also helps Maersk build trust and authority within each of these niche audiences — potential customers, current customers, and even employees.</p> \n<h3>Content Marketing: LeadPages, Blog + Resources</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/integrations/leadpages\">LeadPages</a> has been bootstrapped since its inception in 2012 … yet it hit over $16 million in revenue just three years later. Its owner attributes its rapid success to its content strategy, which makes it a great example of B2B content marketing.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/b2b-marketing-leadpages-blog-content-marketing.png?width=600&amp;name=b2b-marketing-leadpages-blog-content-marketing.png\" alt=\"b2b-marketing-leadpages-blog-content-marketing\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\"><em><span style=\"font-size: 13px;\"><a href=\"https://www.leadpages.net/blog/\">Source</a></span></em></img></p> \n<p>LeadPages produces many different types of content resources, such as a blog, customer stories, a podcast, and a webinar. The variety in these resources allows the company to reach customers where they are using the method that best resonates with them.</p> \n<p>LeadPages offers a blog that covers themes such as A/B testing, lead generation, and other topics that relate to the product and brand, a <a href=\"https://www.leadpages.net/podcast\">weekly podcast</a> that chats with everyday entrepreneurs, and even a <a href=\"https://www.leadpages.net/ultimate-guide-to-landing-pages\">definitive guide to landing pages</a>, which equips its customers to properly use and optimize the LeadPages product — all for free.</p> \n<h3>Social Media Marketing: MailChimp, Instagram</h3> \n<p>Social media is an effective channel on which to engage with your audience. It’s also a fun place to post gorgeous graphics and show off your brand personality. On <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/mailchimp/\">Instagram, MailChimp</a> has excelled at both.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/b2b-marketing-social-media-mailchimp-instagram.png?width=600&amp;name=b2b-marketing-social-media-mailchimp-instagram.png\" alt=\"b2b-marketing-social-media-mailchimp-instagram\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\"><a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/BxHfxo7FmP3/\"></a></img></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 13px;\"><em><a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/BxHfxo7FmP3/\">Source</a></em></p> \n<p>Fewer than half of its Instagram posts have to do with email marketing or the MailChimp product, but the MailChimp team always finds a way to make the posts relevant to its audience and followers — all while featuring fun, engaging, on-brand graphics and videos.</p> \n<p>MailChimp also uses its Instagram to feature real customer stories and testimonials, which can have a big impact on potential consumers in the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-for-every-funnel-stage\">Consideration and Decision stages</a>. Finally, MailChimp makes use of a took called LinkinBio, which allows Instagram users to click-through to its homepage or other digital content (since Instagram doesn’t offer live links on its platform). This creates a clear conversion path for consumers who discover or research MailChimp on Instagram and want to learn more on its website.</p> \n<h2>Invest in B2B Marketing and Reach Your Business Customers</h2> \n<p>Marketing isn’t effective unless you keep your audience in mind, and no other audience is as fickle and critical as business customers. Your marketing should communicate how your business can help theirs … and if it doesn’t, you may as well not be marketing at all.</p> \n<p>Use these tips and strategies to understand your B2B audience, round out your buyer personas, and effectively use B2B marketing strategies that reach them. When you’re focused on your audience, your marketing will do the same.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p></p> \n<img 53A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn22@2020_2/2020/11/14/17-30-24-472_70094b1331220522.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605375018178},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 01:30:18","title":"7 of the Coolest YouTube Banners We've Ever Seen","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-youtube-banners","description":"<p>When someone sends me a really great YouTube video, I always want to know who’s behind it. Was it an ad agency? A small or medium business? A B2B tech company? No matter who it was, if I’m impressed, I want to see more from the content creator.</p> \n<p>So once the video is done, I click the link to visit their profiles.</p> \n<p>And from there, if the brand is really on top of its game, I’ll see its channel art -- the horizontal banner displayed across the top of the user’s YouTube channel that, hopefully, shows a combination of good design and brand presence.</p> \n<p>But how do they do it?</p> \n<p>We’ve all seen design work that inspires us, but can have a bad habit of not taking it any further than that. What makes something like strong YouTube banners so great? And how can you create your own gorgeous artwork? To answer those questions, we found three excellent resources for YouTube banner templates, as well as seven creative channel banners -- both old and new -- that inspire us as marketers.</p> \n<p></p> \n<h2>What Makes a Good YouTube Banner?</h2> \n<h3>Responsive Dimensions</h3> \n<p>A YouTube channel banner will take on different dimensions depending on what platform is being used to view it. For example, a banner might have different dimensions when viewed on a TV, desktop, or mobile device.</p> \n<p><span><a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/2972003?co=GENIE.Platform%3DDesktop&amp;hl=en\">Google</a>'s suggested YouTube banner dimensions are:&nbsp;</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li>Recommended: 2560 x 1440 px</li> \n <li>Minimum for upload: 2048 x 1152 px</li> \n <li>Minimum \"safe area\" where text and logos are ensured not to be cut off: 1546 x 423 px</li> \n <li>Maximum width: 2560 x 423 px</li> \n <li>File size: 4MB or smaller</li> \n</ul> \n<p><span>The recommended resolution&nbsp;</span><span>seems like an exorbitantly large file size. But think about how YouTube banners would appear on a 30\" smart TV or higher. With a growing number of options to view YouTube videos in this way, you'll want to make sure your channel art is large enough to display with quality on larger screens.</span></p> \n<p>Here's a helpful visual representation of those dimensions:</p> \n<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube%20banner%20dimensions.png?width=600&amp;name=youtube%20banner%20dimensions.png\" alt=\"Template showing the dimensions YouTube banners should adhere to\" width=\"600\" title=\"Template showing the dimensions YouTube banners should adhere to\" style=\"width: 600px;\">\n<span style=\"font-size: 12px;\">Source: <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/2972003?co=GENIE.Platform%3DDesktop&amp;hl=en\">Google</a></span> \n<h3>Balanced Design</h3> \n<p>Take note of the \"safe area\" we alluded to in the first section. Your banner is essentially the biggest branding opportunity for when people land on your channel, so you'll want to make sure your logo and supporting text is well-represented in the channel art. That's why it might be best to place your company name and logo in that center space -- this prevents viewer confusion if the name of the company behind the YouTube account is accidentally cut off.</p> \n<p>If you're not sure how to take up the entirety of a 2560 x 1440 frame, video production company <a href=\"https://www.minimatters.com/youtube-channel-art-tips/\">MiniMatters</a> suggests \"build[ing] the image from the middle out,\" putting the most important assets in the center, and going from there.</p> \n<p>Finally, as to what to put in your banner, we like to follow a few basic rules:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Use a high-resolution image. A pixelated or blurry banner doesn't exactly signal that there's high-quality video to follow.</li> \n <li>Keep it on-brand. While your channel art doesn't have to be a carbon copy of your logo or tagline, it should incorporate visual elements that you want associated with your brand, like certain colors, fonts, or keywords.</li> \n <li>Your banner should represent what your company does in a timely fashion. For example, if you run a bakery and you're gearing up for summer, an eye-catching banner might be a high-res photo of a brightly-colored work surface covered with flour and a rolling pin, along with accompanying text like, \"April showers bring May flours.\"</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>How to Make a YouTube Banner</h3> \n<p>\"That's just great, Amanda,\" you might be thinking about these tips. \"But where the heck am I supposed to get these beautiful design assets?\"</p> \n<p>You're in luck -- there are dozens of free resources for creating a great YouTube banner. Here are a few of our favorites:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Google</strong>: Why not start with the hosting platform itself? <a href=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/support-kms-prod/723CF6954B9CC9B50AD58BCC2F5F14825FF4\">Google</a> has its very own channel art templates to help you get started with your banner design. (Note: Clicking this link will prompt an automatic download of the zip file containing these templates.)</li> \n <li><strong>Canva</strong>: One of our go-to destinations for DIY design, <a href=\"https://www.canva.com/create/banners/youtube-banners/\">Canva</a> offers several free YouTube channel art templates that allow you to use your own art, or its library of stock photography.</li> \n <li><strong>Fotor</strong>: Similar to Canva, <a href=\"https://www.fotor.com/features/youtube.html\">Fotor</a> also offers a selection of free YouTube banner templates that allow you to use both your own visual assets or its own library of images.</li> \n</ul> \n<h2>8 Cool YouTube Channel Art Examples</h2> \n<h3>1. Death Wish Coffee Company</h3> \n<img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Death%20Wish%20Coffee%20Company.png?width=669&amp;name=Death%20Wish%20Coffee%20Company.png\" alt=\"Death Wish Coffee Company's YouTube banner\" width=\"669\" title=\"Death Wish Coffee Company's YouTube banner\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> \n<p>In 2016, Death Wish Coffee was named the winner of a small business marketing competition held by software company Intuit. The reward? A <i>free</i> 30-second commercial during Super Bowl 50. Since then, the self-proclaimed maker of “the world’s strongest coffee” has capitalized on that momentum by making sure its branding stays just as robust.</p> \n<p>Its former&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/DeathWishCoffeeCo\">YouTube banner</a>&nbsp;banner is no exception. It’s straightforward, but also, bold. The company’s logo is displayed as the channel icon, as well as a tiled watermark that doesn’t interfere with the text display. And that message doesn’t leave any doubt about what the brand does. “World’s strongest coffee?” Okay, I’m watching.</p> \n<h3>2. Adobe Creative Cloud</h3> \n<img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Adobe%20Creative%20Cloud.png?width=669&amp;name=Adobe%20Creative%20Cloud.png\" alt=\"Adobe Creative Cloud's YouTube banner\" width=\"669\" title=\"Adobe Creative Cloud's YouTube banner\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> \n<p>Seeing as turquoise is my all-time favorite color, there might be a touch of aesthetic bias in our selection of <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/AdobeCreativeCloud\">Adobe Creative Cloud’s YouTube</a> banner. But color can have quite an impact in marketing -- shades of blue, for example, have been found to <a href=\"https://blog.kissmetrics.com/color-psychology/?wide=1\">invoke feelings of trust</a>.</p> \n<p>This banner doesn’t just make great use of color, though. In a single photo, it connotes creativity and visual quality -- two things that the Adobe Creative Cloud promises with its suite products. The person depicted seems to be creating something remarkable -- an ocean inside of a balloon -- with accompanying text to confirm it: “Make wow.” Plus, to learn more, social buttons are right there within the image.</p> \n<h3>3. Bon Appétit</h3> \n<img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Bon%20Appe%CC%81tit.png?width=669&amp;name=Bon%20Appe%CC%81tit.png\" alt=\"Bon Appétit's YouTube banner\" width=\"669\" title=\"Bon Appétit's YouTube banner\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> \n<p>Is anyone else hungry? It only seems right that the channel art for a food magazine like <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/BonAppetitDotCom\"><i>Bon Appétit</i></a> should be, well, appetizing. And with a phrase that’s used as frequently as “bon appétit” -- before a meal or as the title of a pop song -- it’s important that folks who land on this YouTube channel know what they’re getting into.</p> \n<p>That’s one thing that makes this banner so great. The branding is clear, from the logo icon to the iconic title text in the center of the image. Plus, the photo itself sends a signal of the type of content visitors can expect to consume -- no pun intended -- when they start watching the channel’s videos: All things food.</p> \n<h3>4. TauliaInc</h3> \n<img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/TauliaInc.png?width=669&amp;name=TauliaInc.png\" alt=\"TauliaInc's YouTube banner\" width=\"669\" title=\"TauliaInc's YouTube banner\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> \n<p>One great thing about YouTube banners is that they can be swapped out or modified whenever you want, time permitting. That makes them especially conducive to temporary promotions or campaigns. That’s what tech company <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/TauliaInc\">Taulia</a> did for “P2P Superheroes”: a campaign that shows how its software can eliminate difficult, time-consuming tasks, helping everyday professionals focus more on the work that matters and turn them into superheroes.</p> \n<p>The banner communicates two things: 1. That Taulia is in the business of P2P (“procure to pay”), and 2. the brand really celebrates procurement specialists. And by using original, cartoon-like art, Taulia is turning what could be a dry topic into something fun and engaging.</p> \n<h3>5. Refinery29</h3> \n<img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/r29.png?width=669&amp;name=r29.png\" alt=\"Refinery29's YouTube banner\" width=\"669\" title=\"Refinery29's YouTube banner\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> \n<p>We’re big fans of showcasing the people that make your brand great. That’s one thing that <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/Refinery29TV\">Refinery29</a> does well, by frequently featuring its writers, editors, and content producers in its videos. As it turns out, they’ve all become quite popular personalities -- which is why the brand put them front-and-center in its channel art.</p> \n<p>Creating a banner of this nature is two-fold. First, you have to find a way to incorporate your company’s talent into video content in a way that’s engaging and appealing to your target audience. Here at HubSpot, we have our blog writers, for example, recount important information from blog posts in video and audio summaries. Then, once you’ve produced enough of that media consistently -- and if it’s gaining the right kind of attention -- you can use those personalities to promote your channels.</p> \n<h3>6. TripAdvisor B2B</h3> \n<img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/TripAdvisor%20B2B.png?width=669&amp;name=TripAdvisor%20B2B.png\" alt=\"TripAdvisor's YouTube banner\" width=\"669\" title=\"TripAdvisor's YouTube banner\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> \n<p>TripAdvisor is a resource used by millions of travelers to discover and rate lodgings, restaurants, and much more information about endless destinations. But did you know it also offers B2B services for hotel and other property owners to make the most of their presence on the site?</p> \n<p>We like to think of it as a B2B hybrid of review site Yelp and vacation rental site Airbnb. On the one hand, <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCM3TDVOr39aSgx-yyJGz3WA\">TripAdvisor B2B</a> helps business owners create a profile with photos, descriptions, and other information that’s going to be helpful to travelers. But, like Yelp, it also allows them to monitor and respond to the reviews their businesses receive.</p> \n<p>That’s represented in the YouTube banner by portraying what the site is all about -- travel -- but also depicts the act of visitors giving feedback on their experiences by way of rating symbols.</p> \n<h3>7. Nuvolari Lenard</h3> \n<img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/nuvolari%20lenard-1.png?width=669&amp;name=nuvolari%20lenard-1.png\" alt=\"Nuvolari Lenard's YouTube banner\" width=\"669\" title=\"Nuvolari Lenard's YouTube banner\" style=\"width: 669px;\"> \n<p>The thing that stands out to us the most about this banner is its simplicity. It represents a Italian yacht design company <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/nuvolarilenard/feed\">Nuvolari Lenard</a>, which is known for work that emulates a luxury and chic lifestyle. And while the channel art itself doesn’t portray anything specifically nautical, the use of capital letters and tiered monochrome does connote a brand that’s high-end.</p> \n<p>Those kinds of digital aesthetics create what’s often known as aspirational marketing -- the kind that symbolizes something that’s unattainable by most, but still has a vast following of people “who covet the look and feel of the brand,” as <a href=\"http://mediaboom.com/news/5-luxury-brand-marketing-strategies/\">Mediaboom</a> puts it. Can I afford a yacht? Of course not. But seeing something like this makes me want one anyway, and makes me want to consume the video content pertaining to it.</p> \n<h2>Channel Your Creativity</h2> \n<p>It’s important to note that really cool YouTube channel art is just one part of a comprehensive video content strategy. It doesn’t matter how beautiful your banner is, for example, if your channel lacks in quality video, or hasn’t added anything new in several weeks.</p> \n<p>So, along with great design must come consistency. And as you begin to create both, you can turn to these examples for inspiration.</p> \n<p><i>What are some of your favorite YouTube banners? Let us know in the comments.</i></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img
